### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 2 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If 75 percent of the employees of a certain company take a winter vacation, 40 percent take a winter and a summer vacation, and 20 percent take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, what Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation?
Choices:
  A: 5%
  B: 15%
  C: 25%
  D: 35%
  E: 45%
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's say there are 100 employees in the company.
  75% of them take a winter vacation, which means 75 employees take a winter vacation, and 25 employees don't take a winter vacation.
  40% of the employees take both winter and summer vacations, which means 40 employees take both, and 35 employees take only summer vacation or only winter vacation.
  20% of the employees take neither winter nor summer vacation, which means 20 employees don't take either vacation, and 80 employees take at least one of the vacations.
  We want to find the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  Let the percentage of employees who take only a summer vacation be 'x'.
  Then, the percentage of employees who take at least one summer vacation would be 40% + x.
  The percentage of employees who don't take a summer vacation would be 100% - (40% + x) = 60% - x.
  The percentage of employees who take neither vacation is given to be 20%.
  Therefore, we can set up the equation:
  25 + 40 + x + 35 + 20 = 100
  Solving for x, we get x = 15.
  Therefore, 15% of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  The answer is B: 15%.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume that there are 100 employees in total.
  75% of the employees take a winter vacation, which means 75 employees take a winter vacation and 25 employees do not.
  40% of the employees take both a winter and a summer vacation, which means 40 employees take both and 35 employees take only a summer vacation.
  20% of the employees take neither vacation, which means 20 employees do not take either vacation.
  We can calculate the number of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation using the formula (total number of employees who take a summer vacation) - (number of employees who take both vacations).
  The total number of employees who take a summer vacation is 35 + the number of employees who take both vacations.
  So, we need to find the number of employees who take both vacations to calculate the answer.
  We know that 75 employees take a winter vacation and 40 employees take both vacations, which means that 35 employees take only a summer vacation.
  Therefore, the number of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is 35.
  The percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is (35/100) x 100 = 35%.
  The answer is D: 35%.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Let's assume that there are 100 employees in total.
  75% of the employees take a winter vacation, which is 75 employees.
  20% of the employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, which is 20 employees.
  Therefore, 100 - 75 - 20 = 5% of the employees take only a summer vacation.
  40% of the employees take a winter and a summer vacation.
  If we subtract the 40 employees who take a winter and a summer vacation from the 75 employees who take a winter vacation, we get 35% of the employees who take a winter vacation but not a summer vacation.
  Therefore, the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is 5% + 35% = 40%.

Response 3:
Thought:
Let the total number of employees be 100.
Then, 75 employees take a winter vacation (75% of 100).
Let x be the number of employees that take both winter and summer vacations.
Then, 40 employees take both winter and summer vacation (40% of 100).
So, 40 = x + y (where y is the number of employees that take only summer vacation).
20 employees take neither winter nor summer vacation.
Therefore, 100 - (75 + y + x + 20) = 5 - (y + x) employees take only winter vacation.
We want to find the number of employees that take only summer vacation.
Therefore, y employees take only summer vacation.
The number of employees that take a summer vacation is y + x.
So, the percentage of employees that take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is (y + x)/100.
We can solve for y by substituting (40 - x) for y in the equation 40 = x + y.
Then, 40 = x + (40 - x).
So, y = 40 - x.
Substituting this value for y in the expression for the number of employees that take only winter vacation, we get 100 - (75 + 40 - x + 20) = 5 - x.
Solving for x, we get x = 10.
Therefore, y = 40 - x = 30.
So, the number of employees that take a summer vacation is y + x = 30 + 10 = 40.
Therefore, the percentage of employees that take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is (y + x)/100 = 40/100 = 40%.
The answer is E: 40%.

  - 40% of employees take a winter and summer vacation, so the number of employees who take both is 40.

  x = (total number of employees who take at least one vacation) - (number of employees who take neither vacation) - (number of employees who take both)
  x = 80 - 20 - 40 = 20
  So, 20 employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation out of 100 employees.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 3 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular solid, 3 x 4 x 15, is inscribed in a sphere, so that all eight of its vertices are on the sphere. What is the diameter of the sphere?
Choices:
  A:  13.3542
  B:  15.8113
  C:  18.3451
  D:  19.5667
  E:  20.8888
Response 0:
Thought:
  A rectangular solid has 8 vertices.
  The sphere passes through all the vertices of the solid.
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the longest diagonal of the solid.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid with dimensions 3 x 4 x 15 is the diagonal that passes through opposite corners of the solid.
  Using the Pythagorean theorem, the length of the longest diagonal is sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) = sqrt(250).
  Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is sqrt(250) x 2.
  The answer is approximately 15.8113.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is the diameter of the sphere.
  We can find the longest diagonal by applying the Pythagorean Theorem twice.
  The longest diagonal is the square root of the sum of the squares of the three dimensions.
  Diameter of the sphere is the longest diagonal times the square root of 2.
  Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is: sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) * sqrt(2).
  This simplifies to sqrt(9 + 16 + 225) * sqrt(2) = sqrt(250) * sqrt(2) = 5 * sqrt(10) * sqrt(2) = 10 * sqrt(5).
  The answer is E: 20.8888.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Thought:
  The rectangular solid has dimensions of 3 x 4 x 15.
  The sphere is inscribed in the rectangular solid, so the sphere touches the rectangular solid at all eight vertices.
  The diameter of the sphere is the same as the diagonal of the rectangular solid.
  We can use the Pythagorean theorem to find the diagonal of the rectangular solid.
  Diagonal^2 = 3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2
  Diagonal^2 = 9 + 16 + 225
  Diagonal^2 = 250
  Diagonal = sqrt(250)
  Diagonal = 5sqrt(10)
  Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is 2 times the diagonal of the rectangular solid.
  Diameter = 2 * 5sqrt(10)

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 4 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Peter wants to find 10 additional people to form a scavenger hunt team with him. If he has 10 friends who would like to participate, how many choices does he have for forming his team?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 1
  C: 2
  D: 3
  E: 4
Response 0:
Thought:
  Peter wants to choose 10 people from the 10 friends who want to participate.
  The order of the people chosen doesn't matter, so we can use the combination formula.
  The formula for combination is nCr = n! / (r! * (n-r)!)
  Here, n = 10 (number of friends) and r = 10 (number of people to be chosen).
  Plugging in the values, we get 10C10 = 10! / (10! * (10-10)!) = 1.
  Therefore, Peter has only 1 choice for forming his team.
  The answer is B: 1.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Peter has 10 friends to choose from.
  He wants to choose 10 additional people to form a team.
  The order in which he chooses the people doesn't matter.
  Therefore, this is a combination problem.
  He wants to choose 10 people from a pool of 10 friends, without replacement.
  The formula for combinations is nCr = n! / (r! * (n - r)!).
  Plugging in the numbers, we get (10 + 10)C10 = 20C10 = 184,756 choices.
  Therefore, Peter has 184,756 choices for forming his team.
  The answer is None of the Above.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Peter wants to form a team with 10 additional people.
  He has 10 friends who want to participate.
  The order in which the friends are chosen does not matter.
  This is a combination problem because we are choosing a team out of a group of people where order does not matter.
  We can use the combination formula nCr = n! / (r! * (n-r)!).
  We have 10 friends to choose from and need to choose 10 additional people, which is a total of 20 people.
  So, n = 10 and r = 10.
  Plugging these values into the combination formula, we get 10C10 = 10! / (10! * 0!) = 1.
  Therefore, Peter has only 1 choice for forming his team.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 3:
Thought:
Peter wants to find 10 additional people to form a scavenger hunt team with him.
He has 10 friends who would like to participate.
He needs to select 10 people from 10 friends.
The order of selection does not matter as he is forming a team.
This is a combination problem.
The formula for combination is nCr = n! / (r! (n-r)!).
n = 10, r = 10
n! = 10! = 10 x 9 x 8 x 7 x 6 x 5 x 4 x 3 x 2 x 1
r! = 10! = 10 x 9 x 8 x 7 x 6 x 5 x 4 x 3 x 2 x 1
(n-r)! = 0! = 1
nCr = 10! / (10! x 1) = 1
Therefore, Peter has only one choice for forming his team.
The answer is B: 1.

  Here he wants to choose 10 people from a pool of 10, which is 10C10.

Question: An express electric train takes exact three seconds to enter tunnel which is 1 mile long.
If train is traveling at 120 mile an hour, how long will it take to pass completely through the tunnel ?
Choices:
  A: 43 seconds
  B: 39 seconds
  C: 20 seconds
  D: 33 seconds
  E: 55 seconds
Response 0:
Thought:
  The train takes 3 seconds to enter the tunnel, so we can assume it will take 3 seconds to exit.
  The train is traveling at 120 miles per hour, so it covers 1 mile in (1/120) hours.
  We need to find the time it takes to cover the length of the train plus the length of the tunnel.
  Let's assume the length of the train is x miles.
  The total distance the train covers is x + 1 miles.
  We can use the formula: speed = distance / time
  Rearranging the formula to solve for time, we get: time = distance / speed
  Therefore, the time it takes to pass completely through the tunnel is (x + 1) / 120 hours.
  We need to convert this time into seconds.
  1 hour = 60 minutes = 60 x 60 seconds = 3600 seconds.
  Therefore, the time it takes to pass completely through the tunnel is ((x + 1) / 120) x 3600 seconds.
  We know the speed of the train and can calculate its length using the formula: speed = distance / time.
  Rearranging the formula to solve for distance, we get: distance = speed x time.
  Therefore, the length of the train is 0.25 miles (440 yards).
  Now, we can substitute the value of x in the formula for total time to get the answer.
  (x + 1) / 120 = (0.25 + 1) / 120
  x + 1 = 1.25
  x = 0.25
  Therefore, the time it takes to pass completely through the tunnel is (0.25 + 1) / 120 hours = 0.0125 hours = 45 seconds (approx.)

Question: An electric pole, 14 metres high, casts a shadow of 10 metres. Find the height of a tree that casts a shadow of 15 metres under similar conditions.
Choices:
  A: 21
  B: 22
  C: 20
  D: 23
  E: 24
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the height of the tree is 'h'.
  The height of the electric pole is 14m and its shadow is 10m.
  We can set up a proportion to find the height of the tree:
  (Height of the pole) / (Length of its shadow) = (Height of the tree) / (Length of its shadow)
  14 / 10 = h / 15
  Solving for 'h', we get:
  h = (14/10) * 15
  h = 21
  Therefore, the height of the tree is 21 meters.
Action: Answer("A")

  Discount = 20% of x
  Discount = 0.2x
  Selling price after discount = x - 0.2x
  Selling price after discount = 0.8x
  Selling price after discount = (120/100) * Cost price

  0.8x = 960
  x = 1200 + (20/100)*1200 + (20/100)*1200
  x = 1200 + 240 + 240
  x = 1680

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 11 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: At a certain factory, 10 percent of the staplers produced on Monday were defective and 2 percent of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake. If 72 of the non-defective staplers were rejected, what was the number of staplers produced that day?
Choices:
  A: 4,000
  B: 4,200
  C: 4,500
  D: 4,800
  E: 5,000
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the factory produced "x" staplers on Monday.
  10 percent of staplers produced on Monday were defective, so 0.1x staplers were defective.
  The remaining non-defective staplers produced on Monday are (1 - 0.1)x = 0.9x staplers.
  2 percent of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake. We know that 72 non-defective staplers were rejected, so:
  0.02(0.9x) = 72
  0.018x = 72
  x = 4,000
  Therefore, the number of staplers produced that day is 4,000.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Let's assume that the total number of staplers produced on Monday is "x".
  10% of the staplers produced on Monday were defective, which means that 90% of the staplers produced on Monday were non-defective.
  So the number of non-defective staplers produced on Monday is 0.9x.
  2% of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake, which means that 98% of the non-defective staplers were accepted.
  So the number of accepted non-defective staplers is 0.98(0.9x) = 0.882x.
  The number of rejected non-defective staplers is 72.
  The total number of non-defective staplers produced is the sum of the accepted and rejected staplers: 0.882x + 72.
  The total number of staplers produced is the sum of the defective and non-defective staplers: 0.1x + 0.882x + 72 = 0.982x + 72.
  We know that the total number of staplers produced is equal to "x".
  Therefore, we can write the equation: x = 0.982x + 72.
  Solving for "x", we get x = 4,000.
  Therefore, the number of staplers produced that day is 4,000.
  The answer is A: 4,000.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 12 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: M men agree to purchase a gift for Rs. D. If 3 men drop out how much more will each have to contribute towards the purchase of the gift?
Choices:
  A: D/(M-3)
  B: MD/3
  C: M/(D-3)
  D: 3D/(M2-3M)
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  Initially, each man needs to pay D/M rupees for the gift.
  After 3 men drop out, there are M-3 men left to contribute towards the gift.
  The total amount of money needed is still D rupees.
  So, each of the remaining M-3 men needs to pay D/(M-3) rupees for the gift.
  The difference between the amount paid by each man initially and the amount paid after 3 men drop out is:
    D/M - D/(M-3)
  We need to simplify this expression to get the answer.
  We can start by finding the LCM of M and M-3, which is M(M-3).
  Then, we can rewrite the expression using this LCM:
    D/M - D/(M-3) = (D(M-3) - DM)/(M(M-3)) = 3D/(M(M-3))
  Therefore, the answer is D: 3D/(M2-3M).
Action: Answer("D")

Question: The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs?
Choices:
  A: 0.5
  B: 0.6
  C: 0.7
  D: 0.8
  E: 0.9
Response 0:
Thought:
  We know that the probability of A occurring is 0.6.
  We also know that the probability of at least one of the events A or B occurring is 0.96.
  We can use the formula P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B).
  Since A and B are independent, P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B).
  Substituting the given values, we get 0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - 0.6 * P(B).
  Solving for P(B), we get P(B) = 0.8.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 0.8.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  If A and B are independent, then P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B).
  The probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is the complement of the probability that neither A nor B occurs.
  P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B) and P(neither A nor B) = 1 - P(A or B)
  We are given P(A) = 0.6 and P(A or B) = 0.96. We can find P(neither A nor B) and use it to find P(B).
  P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B) => 0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - 0.6P(B) => 0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4P(B) => P(B) = (0.96 - 0.6) / 0.4 = 0.9
  Therefore, the probability that event B occurs is 0.9.

Question: The price of a product is reduced by 30% . By what percentage should it be increased to make it 100%
Choices:
  A: 41.86%
  B: 42.86%
  C: 43.86%
  D: 44.86%
  E: 45.86%

  To increase the new price to 100%, we need to multiply the new price by a factor of (100/70).
  Therefore, the percentage increase is (100/70 - 1) * 100% = 42.86% (rounded to two decimal places).
Action: Answer("B")

Thought:

  The price of the product is reduced by 30%, so the new price is 70% of the original price which is $70.

  Let's assume the percentage increase as x.
  So, the new price after increasing by x% = 70 + (x/100)*70.
  We need to find the value of x so that 70 + (x/100)*70 = 100.
  Solving the equation, we get x = 42.86.
  Therefore, the percentage increase required is 42.86%.
  The answer is B: 42.86%.

Question: A flagstaff 17.5 metre high casts a shadow of length 40.25 metre. The height of building, which casts a shadow of length 28.75 metre under similar conditions will be :
Choices:
  A: 12 metre
  B: 12.5 metre
  C: 13.5 metre
  D: 14 metre
  E: 15 metre
Response 0:
Thought:
  The height of the flagstaff is 17.5 metre and it casts a shadow of length 40.25 metre.
  Let the height of the building be x metre which casts a shadow of length 28.75 metre.
  Since the conditions are similar, the ratios of corresponding sides of the two triangles will be equal.
  Therefore, (Height of flagstaff / Length of shadow of flagstaff) = (Height of building / Length of shadow of building)
  (17.5 / 40.25) = (x / 28.75)
  x = (17.5 x 28.75) / 40.25
  x = 12.5
  Therefore, the height of the building is 12.5 metre.
  The answer is B: 12.5 metre.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume the height of the building is 'h'.

  height of the flagstaff / its shadow length = height of the building / its shadow length
  17.5 / 40.25 = h / 28.75
  Solving for 'h':
  h = (17.5 x 28.75) / 40.25
  h = 12.5

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 20 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An exam is given in a certain class. The average (arithmetic mean) of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. If the average score for the entire class is equal to y and there are z students in the class, where z > 5, then in terms of x, y, and z, what is the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers?
Choices:
  A: (zy – 2x)/z
  B: (zy – 2)/z
  C: (zx – y)/(z – 2)
  D: (zy – 2x)/(z -2)
  E: (zy – x)/(z + 2)
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the lowest score is L and the highest score is H. 
  We know that the average of the highest and lowest scores is (L+H)/2 = x.
  We also know that the average score for the entire class is y.
  The sum of all scores is (z)(y).
  We need to find the sum of all scores excluding the highest and lowest scores.
  This is (z-2) multiplied by the average score of the class.
  We can write this relationship as:
  (z-2) * average score = (z*y) - L - H
  We can substitute (L+H)/2 for x to get:
  (z-2) * average score = (z*y) - 2x
  Solving for the average score, we get:
  average score = (zy - 2x)/(z-2)
  Therefore, the answer is D: (zy - 2x)/(z-2).
Action: Answer("D")

  This is equal to (s - a - b)/(z - 2).

  We can express a and b in terms of x and the sum of the remaining scores, which we'll call r.
  We know that (a + b)/2 = x, so a + b = 2x.
  We also know that r/z-2 = y.
  Solving for r, we get r = y(z - 2).
  Substituting a + b = 2x and r = y(z - 2) into (s - a - b)/(z - 2), we get (yz - 2x - y(z - 2))/(z - 2).
  Simplifying this expression, we get (zy - 2x)/(z - 2).
  Therefore, the answer is D: (zy – 2x)/(z -2).

  B: 60%
  C: 70%
  D: 86%
  E: 90%
Response 0:
Thought:
  The astronaut weighs 211 pounds on Earth and 182 pounds on Venus.
  The percentage of the astronaut's weight on Venus compared to Earth is (182/211) * 100% = 86% (rounded to the nearest whole number).
  Therefore, the answer is D: 86%.

Question: At its maximum speed, a space shuttle can travel 700m high in 40 seconds. It will also take 5 seconds to pass a point. What then is the length of the space shuttle?
Choices:
  A: 50 m
  B: 75 m
  C: 100 m
  D: 125 m
  E: 150 m
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can use the formula: distance = speed x time
  The shuttle travels 700m in 40 seconds, so its speed is 700/40 = 17.5 m/s.
  In 5 seconds, the shuttle will travel 17.5 x 5 = 87.5 m to pass a point.
  The length of the shuttle is the distance it covers during the 5 seconds when it passes the point minus the height it gains during that time.
  The height it gains during that time is speed x time = 17.5 x 5 = 87.5 m.
  Therefore, the length of the shuttle is 87.5 m - 700 m = -612.5 m.
  Since the answer must be positive, the length of the shuttle is not valid.
  None of the choices is correct.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 24 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced. If the yard has an area of 240 square meters, how many meters of fencing does she need?
Choices:
  A: 58
  B: 62
  C: 66
  D: 70
  E: 74
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's assume the length of the yard is L and the width of the yard is W.
  The area of the yard is given as L * W = 240.
  One side of the yard is 10 meters unfenced. Let's assume that's the length of the yard.
  The perimeter of the yard is P = L + W + L = 2L + W.
  We need to find the perimeter of the yard to calculate the amount of fencing needed.
  We can solve for W using the area of the yard equation: W = 240/L.
  Substituting W back into the perimeter equation, we get P = 2L + 240/L.
  We can find the value of L by differentiating the perimeter equation with respect to L and setting it to zero to find the minimum value of P.
  Differentiating, we get dP/dL = 2 - 240/L^2 = 0. Solving for L, we get L = sqrt(120).
  Substituting L back into the perimeter equation, we get P = 2*sqrt(120) + 20 = 2*2*sqrt(30) + 20 = 4*sqrt(30) + 20.
  Therefore, Alice needs 4*sqrt(30) + 20 meters of fencing.
  Rounding off to the nearest whole number, the answer is 66 meters.
  The answer is C: 66.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's suppose the length of the yard is "l" and the width is "w".
  We know that the area of a rectangle is given by: A = l * w
  We are given that the area of the yard is 240 square meters.
  Therefore, l * w = 240
  
  We also know that Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of the yard.
  This means that there will be fencing along the perimeter of the yard, except for one side of 10 meters.
  We need to find the perimeter of the yard.
  
  The perimeter of a rectangle is given by: P = 2l + 2w
  Since one side (w) has no fencing, we only need to find the perimeter of the other three sides.
  P = l + 2w
  
  We need to substitute the value of w in terms of l using the area equation:
  w = 240 / l
  
  Therefore:
  P = l + 2 * (240 / l)
  
  To minimize the amount of fencing needed, we need to find the value of l that minimizes P.
  We can do this by finding the derivative of P with respect to l, setting it equal to zero, and solving for l.
  After some calculus, we get:
  l^2 = 480
  l = sqrt(480) = 4 * sqrt(30)
  
  Now we can find the perimeter:
  P = l + 2 * (240 / l) = 4 * sqrt(30) + 2 * sqrt(30) = 6 * sqrt(30)
  
  Therefore, Alice needs 6 * sqrt(30) meters of fencing.
  We can approximate this value to the nearest integer:
  6 * sqrt(30) ≈ 62.09
  The closest answer choice is B: 62.

Topic: Math
Question: A sporting goods store carries only yellow and white golf balls. At the beginning of the day it had 600 golf balls in stock, and by the end of the day it had sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls. If the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, and in doing so sold all of its white golf balls, how many yellow golf balls did the store have to begin the day?
Choices:
  A: 80
  B: 120
  C: 240
  D: 320
  E: 360
Response 0:
Thought:
  The store sold 80% of its inventory, so it sold 0.8 * 600 = 480 golf balls.
  Since the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, it sold 240 white golf balls.
  Therefore, the store had 600 - 240 = 360 yellow golf balls to begin the day.
  The answer is E: 360.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The store sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls.
  If the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, then 50% of its inventory was yellow golf balls.
  Therefore, the store began the day with 50% of 600 golf balls, or 300 yellow golf balls.
  The answer is 300.
Action: Answer("None of the above")

- Therefore, 20% of the golf balls remaining must be yellow golf balls.

- Therefore, the store had 120 yellow golf balls at the beginning of the day.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 26 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The bus fare for two persons for travelling between Agra and Aligarh id four-thirds the train fare between the same places for one person. The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train between the two places is Rs.1512. Find the train fare between the two places for one person?
Choices:
  A: 126
  B: 77
  C: 88
  D: 66
  E: 54
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's assume that the train fare for one person is X.
Then, the bus fare for two persons will be 4/3 X.
The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus is (4/3 X) * 3 = 4X.
The total fare paid by 8 persons travelling by train is X * 8 = 8X.
The sum of these two fares is given as Rs.1512.
Therefore, 4X + 8X = 1512.
Simplifying the equation, we get 12X = 1512.
Thus, the value of X, which is the train fare for one person, is X = 126.
Therefore, the answer is A: 126.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:

  The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train between the two places is Rs.1512.
  Therefore, 8x + 8x = 1512  =>  x = 94.5
  The train fare between the two places for one person is Rs. 94.5.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 27 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Jim filled his dog's bowl with dog food. Starting at 8:00 am, Jim's dog ate exactly once an hour, consuming exactly 1/3 of the dog food remaining in the bowl at each feeding session. Approximately, what percent of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon of the same day?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 25%
  C: 30%
  D: 35%
  E: 40%
Response 0:
Thought:
  Jim's dog eats 1/3 of the remaining food every hour, which means that 2/3 of the original food is left after each feeding session.
  From 8:00 am to 12:00 pm, Jim's dog ate four times.
  Therefore, the amount of dog food remaining in the bowl at noon is (2/3)^4 of the original amount.
  (2/3)^4 = 16/81
  This means that approximately 19.75% of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon.
  The closest answer choice is 20%, so the answer is A: 20%.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Starting at 8:00 am, the dog ate once an hour for 4 hours until noon.
  At each feeding session, the dog consumed 1/3 of the remaining food.
  Therefore, the amount of food remaining after each feeding can be represented as (2/3)^n, where n is the number of hours since 8:00 am.
  The amount of food remaining before the dog began to eat at noon is (2/3)^4, which is approximately 19.07%.
  Therefore, approximately 19.07% of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Starting from 8:00 am to 12:00 pm, the dog ate for 4 hours.
  The dog ate exactly once every hour, so the dog ate 4 times.

  Let F be the amount of food in the bowl at 8:00 am.
  At 9:00 am, the dog ate 1/3 of F, so 2/3 of F remained.
  At 10:00 am, the dog ate 1/3 of 2/3 of F, so 4/9 of F remained.
  At 11:00 am, the dog ate 1/3 of 4/9 of F, so 8/27 of F remained.
  At 12:00 pm, the dog ate 1/3 of 8/27 of F, so 16/81 of F remained.
  Therefore, 16/81 of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon.
  To convert this fraction to a percentage, we can divide 16 by 81 and multiply by 100.
  16/81 = 0.1975, so approximately 20% of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon.
  The answer is A: 20%.

Question: Anna is able to buy 5 more articles for $300 after the price of each article decreased by 15%. What is the new selling price of each article?
Choices:
  A: $8
  B: $10
  C: $13.6
  D: $22.9
  E: $40

  Let the original price of each article be x.
  After a 15% decrease, the new price of each article is 0.85x.
  We know that Anna can buy 5 more articles at the new price, so:
  5(0.85x) = $60
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = $11.76
  Therefore, the new selling price of each article is 0.85x = $9.9996, which is approximately $10.
  The answer is B: $10.

  If Anna can buy 5 more articles for $300, then she was originally going to buy 5 fewer articles for $300.
  Let x be the original price of each article.
  The original total cost of the articles was x*(n-5), where n is the original number of articles.
  Since the price of each article decreased by 15%, the new price of each article is 0.85x.
  The new total cost of the articles is 0.85x*n = x*(n-5)+300.
  We can solve for x to find the new selling price of each article.
  Simplifying the equation gives 0.15xn = 300+5x.
  Dividing both sides by n gives 0.15x = (300+5x)/n.
  Multiplying both sides by 20/n gives 3x/n = 60/n+x/n.
  Simplifying gives x/n = $8, which is the new selling price of each article.

Question: A rope 20 meters long is cut into two pieces. If the length of one piece of rope is 3 meters shorter than the length of the other, what is the length, in meters, of the longer piece of rope?

  B: 8.9
  C: 9.9
  D: 11.5
  E: 11.7

  Simplifying the equation, we get 2x = 23.
  Hence, x = 11.5 meters.
  Therefore, the length of the longer piece of rope is 11.5 meters.

Question: In a survey of students, each student selected from a list of 10 songs the 2 songs that the student liked best. If each song was selected 5 times, how many students were surveyed?
Choices:
  A: 96
  B: 48
  C: 32
  D: 25
  E: 18
Response 0:
Thought:
  If each of the 10 songs was selected 5 times, there were a total of 10 x 5 = 50 selections.
  Each student selected 2 songs, so the number of students surveyed is 50/2 = 25.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 25.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Each student selected 2 songs from a list of 10 songs.
  Therefore, there were 10 choose 2 ways to select 2 songs, which is equal to (10!)/(2!*(10-2)!) = 45 ways.
  Each song was selected 5 times.
  Therefore, there were a total of 45*5 = 225 selections.
  Each student made 2 selections, so the number of students surveyed is 225/2 = 112.5.
  The number of students surveyed must be a positive integer, so the answer is either 96 or 48.
  112.5 is closer to 96 than to 48.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 96.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 31 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The original retail price of an appliance was 60 percent more than its wholesale cost. If the appliance was actually sold for 20 percent less than the original retail price, then it was sold for what percent more than its wholesale cost?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 28%
  C: 36%
  D: 40%
  E: 42%
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the wholesale cost of the appliance is $100.
  The original retail price of the appliance is 60% more than the wholesale cost, which is $100 + 60%($100) = $160.
  The appliance was sold for 20% less than the original retail price, which is $160 - 20%($160) = $128.
  The difference between the selling price and the wholesale cost is $128 - $100 = $28.
  The percent more than the wholesale cost is ($28/$100) × 100% = 28%.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 28%.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let the wholesale cost of the appliance be x.
The original retail price of the appliance is 60% more than its wholesale cost, which is 1.6x.
The appliance was sold for 20% less than the original retail price, which is 0.8(1.6x) = 1.28x.
The percent increase from the wholesale cost to the final selling price is [(final selling price - wholesale cost) / wholesale cost] x 100%.
Substituting the values, we get [(1.28x - x) / x] x 100% = 28%.
Therefore, the answer is B: 28%.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 32 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: When folded into two equal halves a rectangular sheet had a perimeter of 48cm for each part folded along one set of sides and the same is 66cm when folded along the other set of sides. Find the area of the sheet.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 1120
  C: 792
  D: 1320
  E: 1200
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the length of the rectangle be l and the breadth be b.
  When folded along the length, the perimeter of each part is 48cm.
  Therefore, the length of each part is 24cm (since there are two parts).
  When folded along the breadth, the perimeter of each part is 66cm.
  Therefore, the breadth of each part is 33cm (since there are two parts).
  The length of the rectangle is the sum of the length of the two parts, which is 48cm.
  The breadth of the rectangle is the sum of the breadth of the two parts, which is 66cm.
  Therefore, we have the equations:
  2l = 48 and 2b = 66
  Solving for l and b, we get l = 24 and b = 33.
  The area of the rectangle is l*b = 24*33 = 792.
  The answer is C: 792.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Let the length and breadth of the rectangular sheet be l and b respectively.
  When folded along one set of sides, the perimeter of each part is 48cm.
  Therefore, 2(l+b/2) = 48, which simplifies to l+b = 48/2*2 = 24.
  When folded along the other set of sides, the perimeter of each part is 66cm.
  Therefore, 2(l/2+b) = 66, which simplifies to l+b = 66/2*2 = 33.
  We now have two equations: l+b=24 and l+b=33.
  Subtracting one equation from the other, we get l = 33-24 = 9.
  Then, b = 24-l = 15.
  Therefore, the area of the rectangular sheet is l*b = 9*15 = 135.
  The answer is not among the choices.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 33 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: On a normal day Bill usually averages about 15 mph when riding his bicycle. On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph. How far can Bill travel on a windy day in 21 minutes? Round to the nearest hundredth.
Choices:
  A: 2 miles
  B: 2.25 miles
  C: 3.25 miles
  D: 3.85 miles
  E: 2.85 miles
Response 0:
Thought:
  Bill's speed on a normal day is 15 mph.
  On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph, so his speed would be 11 mph.
  Bill wants to travel for 21 minutes on a windy day.
  We need to convert minutes to hours so that we can use the speed in mph.
  21 minutes is equal to 0.35 hours (21/60 = 0.35).
  We can use the formula: distance = speed x time.
  Therefore, distance = 11 mph x 0.35 hours = 3.85 miles (rounded to the nearest hundredth).
  The answer is D: 3.85 miles.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  On a normal day, Bill averages 15 mph.
  On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph, so he travels at 11 mph.
  We need to find how far he can travel in 21 minutes, which is 0.35 hours.

Question: In a bag of red and green sweets, the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4. If the bag contains 120 green sweets, how many red sweets are there?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 80
  C: 95
  D: 100
  E: 85
Response 0:
Thought:
  The ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4.
  This means that for every 3 red sweets, there are 4 green sweets.
  We know that there are 120 green sweets.
  Using the ratio, we can set up a proportion to solve for the number of red sweets.
  Let x be the number of red sweets. 
  Then we have: 
  3/4 = x/120
  Cross-multiplying, we get:
  4x = 3 * 120
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = 90
  Therefore, there are 90 red sweets.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

  Let x be the number of red sweets in the bag.

  Multiplying both sides by 120 gives x = 360/7, which is approximately 51.4.

Topic: Math
Question: A number of friends decided to go on a picnic and planned to spend Rs. 96 on eatables. Four of them, however, did not turn up. As a consequence, the remaining ones had to contribute Rs. 4 extra, each. The number of those who attended the picnic was
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 12
  C: 16
  D: 24
  E: 25
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's suppose initially there were 'x' people who decided to go on a picnic.
The cost per person would be 96/x.
Since 4 people did not turn up, now the cost per person increased by Rs. 4.
So, new cost per person = 96/(x-4) = (96/x) + 4.
On solving this equation, we get x= 12.
Therefore, the number of those who attended the picnic was initially 12.
The answer is B: 12.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
Let's assume that the number of friends who initially decided to go on a picnic is x.
The total amount they planned to spend was Rs. 96.
Thus, each friend would have contributed 96/x rupees.
Later, 4 of them did not turn up, so the remaining friends had to contribute Rs. 4 extra each. 
So, now each of the remaining (x-4) friends contributed (96/x) + 4 rupees.
The total amount collected after they contributed extra was Rs. 96.
Therefore, we can create an equation: (96/x) + 4(x-4) = 96.
Simplifying it, we get: x^2 - 16x + 48 = 0.
This equation can be factored as (x-12)(x-4) = 0.
Thus, the possible values of x are 12 and 4.
However, 4 friends did not turn up, so the answer should be 12.
Therefore, the number of those who attended the picnic was 12.
The answer is B: 12.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 37 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: there are more than 501 students in a school such that 20% of them exactly took physics and 28% of them exactly took math. What could be the least possible no of students in the school?
Choices:
  A: 550
  B: 570
  C: 600
  D: 700
  E: none of these
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's assume that the total number of students is N.
From the question, we know that:
- 20% of the students took Physics, which means there are 0.2N students who took Physics.
- 28% of the students took Math, which means there are 0.28N students who took Math.
We can add these two expressions to get the total number of students who took either Physics or Math:
0.2N + 0.28N = 0.48N
We know that this number is greater than 501, so we can write:
0.48N > 501
N > 501/0.48
N > 1043.75
We need to find the least possible number of students, so we can round up to the nearest integer:
N >= 1044
Therefore, the least possible number of students in the school is 1044.
The answer is not among the choices given, so the most likely answer is E: none of these.

  Therefore, the total number of students who took physics is 0.2x and the total number of students who took math is 0.28x.
  We know that the total number of students in the school is more than 501, so we can set up an inequality: x > 501.
  We want to find the least possible value of x that satisfies both the inequality and the conditions on the percentages of students who took physics and math.
  We can use the fact that the percentages must add up to less than 100% to set up another inequality: 0.2x + 0.28x < 100.
  Simplifying this inequality, we get: 0.48x < 100.
  Dividing both sides by 0.48, we get: x < 208.33.
  Since x must be an integer (it represents the number of students), the smallest possible value of x that satisfies both inequalities is 570.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 570.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 38 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Two cars are travelling from the same starting point in the same direction, having started their commute at the same time. The first car travels at a steady rate of 55 mph, while the second travels at a steady rate of 52 mph. How much time will pass before the cars are 15 miles away from each other?
Choices:
  A: 3 hours
  B: 5 hours
  C: 6 hours
  D: 4 hours
  E: 7 hours
Response 0:
Thought:
  The cars are travelling in the same direction and the faster car is travelling at a speed of 55 mph.
  The slower car is travelling at a speed of 52 mph.
  Therefore, the relative speed between the cars is 55 mph - 52 mph = 3 mph.
  We need to find how much time it takes for the distance between the cars to be 15 miles.
  Distance = Speed x Time
  Time = Distance / Speed
  Time = 15 miles / 3 mph = 5 hours
  Therefore, the answer is B: 5 hours.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The distance between the two cars is decreasing at a rate of 55 mph - 52 mph = 3 mph.
  We want to know how long it will take for the distance between the two cars to be 15 miles.
  We can use the formula: time = distance / rate.
  We can set up the equation (time for both cars will be the same):
  15 miles / 3 mph = 5 hours.
  Therefore, it will take 5 hours for the cars to be 15 miles away from each other.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  The rate at which the distance between the two cars increases is the difference between their speeds (55 mph - 52 mph = 3 mph).
  We need to calculate how long it takes for the distance between the cars to be 15 miles.
  We can use the formula: distance = rate x time.
  Let's assume t is the time (in hours) it takes for the cars to be 15 miles apart. 
  The distance travelled by the second car in that time would be 52t miles.
  The distance travelled by the first car would be 55t miles.
  The difference between the distances travelled by the two cars would be 55t - 52t = 3t miles.
  We want the difference between the distances to be 15 miles, so we set up the equation: 
  3t = 15 
  Solving for t, we get t = 5.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 5 hours.

  B: 24
  C: 48
  D: 20
  E: 36

  Therefore, he can eat breakfast and dinner in 6 x 8 = 48 different ways.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 40 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Suppose for any real number x, [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x. Let L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y] and R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]. Then it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers x and y for which
Choices:
  A: L(x,y) = R(x,y)
  B: L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y)
  C: L(x,y) < R(x,y)
  D: L(x,y) < R(x,y)
  E: None
Response 0:
Thought: 
  [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x.
  [y] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to y.
  [x+y] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x+y.
  [2x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to 2x.
  [2y] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to 2y.
  Since the greatest integer less than or equal to any real number is an integer, both L(x,y) and R(x,y) are sums of integers.
  Therefore, L(x,y) and R(x,y) are integers.
  It is impossible for two different integers to be equal to each other.
  Therefore, it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers x and y for which L(x,y) = R(x,y).
  Thus, the answer is A: L(x,y) = R(x,y).
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x.
  L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y]
  R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]
  Let's try to find a pair of positive real numbers x and y such that L(x,y) = R(x,y).
  Since [x] and [y] are integers, and [x + y] is an integer, we can write [x + y] as [x + y] = [2(x + y)/2].
  Therefore, we can write L(x,y) as L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [2(x + y)/2].
  Since [2x] and [2y] are integers, we can write R(x,y) as R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y] = [2(x + y) - (x + y)] + [2(x + y) - x - y].
  Therefore, we can write R(x,y) as R(x,y) = [2(x + y)/2] + [2(x + y)/2 - x] + [2(x + y)/2 - y].
  Since [x] and [y] are integers, we have x - 1 < [x] ≤ x and y - 1 < [y] ≤ y.
  Therefore, we have x + y - 2 < [x] + [y] ≤ x + y.

  Since [x + y] is an integer, we have [x + y] = x + y - l, where l is an integer such that 0 ≤ l < 1.
  Therefore, we have L(x,y) = x + y - l - k.
  Since [2x] and [2y] are integers, we have 2x - 1 < [2x] ≤ 2x and 2y - 1 < [2y] ≤ 2y.
  Therefore, we have 4x + 4y - 6 < [2x] + [2y] ≤ 4x + 4y.

  Therefore, we have R(x,y) ≤ 2x + 2y - 2.
  Since x and y are positive real numbers, we have L(x,y) < R(x,y).

Thought:
  Let's try to simplify the expressions L(x,y) and R(x,y).
  [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x.
  [y] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to y.
  [x + y] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x + y.
  [2x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to 2x.
  [2y] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to 2y.
  Let's assume that x = a + b and y = c + d, where a, b, c, and d are non-negative real numbers less than 1.
  Then [x] = a, [y] = c, [x + y] = a + c if a + c < 1, otherwise [x + y] = a + c - 1.
  Also, [2x] = 2a if a < 0.5, otherwise [2x] = 2a - 1.
  Similarly, [2y] = 2c if c < 0.5, otherwise [2y] = 2c - 1.
  Therefore, L(x,y) = a + c + [a + b + c + d] if a + c + b + d < 1, otherwise L(x,y) = a + c + [a + b + c + d - 1].
  And R(x,y) = 2a + 2c if a + c < 0.5, otherwise R(x,y) = 2a + 2c - 1.
  Now, let's consider each choice.
  A: L(x,y) = R(x,y). This means that either a + c + b + d < 1 and 2a + 2c = a + c + [a + b + c + d], or a + c + b + d ≥ 1 and 2a + 2c - 1 = a + c + [a + b + c + d - 1]. In the first case, we get a + c = [a + b + c + d], which implies that b + d < 1. But then 2a + 2c = 2[a + c], which means that a + c = [a + c], a contradiction. In the second case, we get 2a + 2c - a - c = [a + b + c + d - 1], which simplifies to a + c = [a + b + c + d - 1] + 1/2. But this is impossible, as a + c is an integer and [a + b + c + d - 1] + 1/2 is not.
  B: L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y). This is true, as shown by case A.
  C: L(x,y) < R(x,y). This means that either a + c + b + d < 1 and 2a + 2c > a + c + [a + b + c + d], or a + c + b + d ≥ 1 and 2a + 2c - 1 > a + c + [a + b + c + d - 1]. In the first case, we get a + c > [a + b + c + d], which implies that b + d > 0. But then 2a + 2c > 2[a + c], which means that a + c < [a + c], a contradiction. In the second case, we get 2a + 2c - a - c > [a + b + c + d - 1], which simplifies to a + c > [a + b + c + d - 1] + 1/2. But this is true, since a + c is an integer and [a + b + c + d - 1] + 1/2 is not.
  D: L(x,y) > R(x,y). This is false, since L(x,y) is always less than or equal to R(x,y), as shown by case C.
  E: None. The answer is C: L(x,y) < R(x,y).
Action: Answer("C")
Response 9:
Thought:
  [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x.
  Therefore, [x] ≤ x.
  [y] ≤ y.
  [x + y] ≤ x + y.
  [2x] ≤ 2x.
  [2y] ≤ 2y.
  Adding the above inequalities, we get:
  [x] + [y] + [x + y] + [2x] + [2y] ≤ 5(x + y).
  Since L(x,y) and R(x,y) are integers, we have:
  L(x,y) ≤ [x] + [y] + [x + y] + [2x] + [2y] ≤ R(x,y) + 5.
  If we can find x and y such that L(x,y) = R(x,y), that would mean:
  [x] + [y] + [x + y] + [2x] + [2y] = [2x] + [2y].
  Simplifying, we get:
  [x] + [y] + [x + y] = [2x] + [2y] - [x] - [y] - [x + y].
  [x] + [y] + [x + y] = [2x] + [2y] - [x + y].
  [x] + [y] + [x + y] = [2x + 2y] - [x + y].
  [x] + [y] + [x + y] + [x + y] = [2x + 2y] + [x + y].
  Simplifying, we get:
  [2x + 2y] = [4x + 4y].
  Since 2x + 2y < 4x + 4y < 2x + 2y + 2, we get:
  [2x + 2y] = [4x + 4y] = 2x + 2y.
  Therefore, we can find x and y such that L(x,y) = R(x,y).
  The answer is not A.
  Since we have shown that L(x,y) ≤ R(x,y) + 5, we can find x and y such that L(x,y) > R(x,y).
  The answer is not C.
  Since we have shown that L(x,y) ≤ R(x,y) + 5, we can find x and y such that L(x,y) < R(x,y) + 5.

Question: While selling a watch, a shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%. If he gives a discount of 7%, he earns Rs. 15 less as profit. The marked price of the watch is:
Choices:
  A: Rs. 697.50
  B: Rs. 712.50
  C: Rs. 787.50
  D: Rs. 750
  E: Rs. 780
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the marked price of the watch is 'x' Rs.
  When the shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%, he earns a profit of (100-5)% = 95% of the marked price.
  When the shopkeeper gives a discount of 7%, he earns a profit of (100-7)% = 93% of the marked price.
  According to the problem, the difference in profit is Rs. 15.
  Therefore, (95/100)*x - (93/100)*x = 15
  Solving the above equation, we get x = Rs. 750
  Therefore, the marked price of the watch is Rs. 750.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's assume that the cost price of the watch is C and the marked price is M.
The selling price of the watch after a discount of 5% is 0.95M.
The selling price of the watch after a discount of 7% is 0.93M.
The profit made by selling the watch at a discount of 5% is (0.95M - C).
The profit made by selling the watch at a discount of 7% is (0.93M - C).
According to the problem, (0.95M - C) = (0.93M - C) + 15.
By solving the above equation, we get M = 750.
Therefore, the marked price of the watch is Rs. 750.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:

  That means the difference between the profit earned with a 5% discount and the profit earned with a 7% discount is Rs. 15.
  Let the profit earned with a 5% discount be P.
  Then, the profit earned with a 7% discount will be P - 15.
  Profit is calculated as the difference between the selling price and the cost price.
  Let the cost price of the watch be C.
  We can write two equations based on the above information:
  0.95M - C = P   ....(1)
  0.93M - C = P - 15   ....(2)
  Subtracting equation (1) from (2), we get:
  0.02M = 15
  M = 750
  Therefore, the marked price of the watch is Rs. 750.

Question: I have a money pouch containing Rs. 700. There are equal number of 25 paise coins, 50 paise coins and one rupee coins.
How many of each are there?
Choices:
  A: 453
  B: 651
  C: 400
  D: 487
  E: 286
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that there are 'x' number of each coin.
  Then, the total amount of money in the pouch is:
  Total amount = (25/100)x + (50/100)x + 1x
  Total amount = (3/4)x + (1)x
  Total amount = (7/4)x
  We know that the total amount of money is Rs. 700.
  Therefore:
  (7/4)x = 700
  Multiplying both sides by (4/7), we get:
  x = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 coins of each denomination.
  The answer is C: 400.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 43 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is:
Choices:
  A: 2.6m
  B: 3.9m
  C: 4m
  D: 4.2m
  E: 4.4m
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the height of the room be 2x.
  Let the semi-perimeter of the room be 5y.
  Let the length, breadth, and height of the room be l, b, and 2x respectively.
  The cost of papering the walls is given as Rs.260. The cost of the paper is Rs.2 per meter.
  The area of the doors and windows is given as 15 sq.m.
  The area of the four walls of the room is 2x(2y+l) = 4xy + 2xl.
  The area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m.
  The area of the paper required to cover the walls is (4xy + 2xl - 15) x 0.5.
  The cost of the paper required to cover the walls is 2 x (4xy + 2xl - 15) = 8xy + 4xl - 30.
  We have two equations in x and y:
    i) 2x/5y = 2/5 => 2y = 5x
    ii) 8xy + 4xl - 30 = 260
  Solving these equations, we get x = 2.6.
  Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 5.2m.
  The answer is not one of the given choices.
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5y.
  Then, the perimeter of the room is 2(2x) + 2(5y) = 4x + 10y.
  We know that the height of the room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5, so we can write:
  (2x) / (5y) = 2 / 5
  Cross-multiplying, we get:
  10x = 10y
  x = y
  Therefore, the perimeter of the room is 4x + 10x = 14x.
  Let the length and breadth of the room be l and b, respectively.
  Then, we have:
  2x * l + 2x * b = 2lb = area of the four walls
  Let the height of the four walls be h.
  Then, we have:
  h * 50 * 0.01 = Rs.260 - 15 * 2 = Rs.230
  h = 4.6
  The height of the room is h + 2x = 4.6 + 2(2x) = 4.6 + 4x.
  We need to find x.
  Let's solve for x using the equation we got earlier:
  10x = 10y
  10x = 2x * 5y / 2x
  10x = 5y
  x = y / 2
  Semi-perimeter = 5y = 10x
  Perimeter = 14x
  Perimeter = 2 * (length + breadth)
  14x = 2(l + b)
  l + b = 7x
  We also know that the area of the four walls is 2lb.
  Area of the four walls = 2lb = 4x(l + b) = 4x(7x) = 28x^2
  We are given that the area of the four walls is 230/2 = 115.
  Therefore, we can write:
  28x^2 = 115
  x^2 = 115/28
  x = sqrt(115/28)
  x = 1.657
  The height of the room is 4.6 + 4x = 4.6 + 4 * 1.657 = 11.548
  Rounding off to one decimal place, we get the height of the room as 11.5.
  Therefore, the answer is none of the above.
  The closest option is E: 4.4m.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Let the height of the room be 2x and semi-perimeter be 5x.
  Then, perimeter = 10x and width of the room = (area of four walls)/(height of the room + height of the room to semi-perimeter ratio) = (260*100)/(2*5*2) = 2600/20 = 130cm = 1.3m
  Area of four walls = width of the room * height of the room * 2 + length of the room * height of the room * 2
  Length of the room = (perimeter - width of the room)/2 = (10x - 1.3)/2
  Area of four walls = 2*1.3*2x + 2*(10x-1.3)*2x = 52x^2 - 10.8x
  Area of doors and windows = 15 sq.m

  Cost of papering = (total area to be covered with paper * 2)/100 * 2 = (104x^2 - 21.6x - 30)/10
  (104x^2 - 21.6x - 30)/10 = 260
  104x^2 - 21.6x - 3000 = 0

  Since height cannot be negative, x = 2.5
  Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 5m.

  The cost of papering the four walls can be calculated as (8x^2 - 15) * 4 * 2 / 100 = (64x^2 - 60) / 5.
  According to the question, (64x^2 - 60) / 5 = 260.
  Solving for x, we get x = 3.5.
  Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 7m.

  Then, the other two sides of the room are 5y/2 - x and 5y/2 + x.
  The cost of papering the wall is the product of the length of the wall and the cost per meter.
  The length of the wall is the sum of the lengths of the other two sides multiplied by the height of the room.
  The area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m, which is subtracted from the total area of the wall to get the area to be papered. 
  Using the given information, we can form two equations in terms of x and y, and solve them to get the value of x.
  The height of the room is 2x, which we can calculate once we have the value of x.
  
Working:
Let the height of the room be 2x and semi-perimeter be 5y.

Then, we have:
2x : 5y = 2 : 5
10x = 2 * 5y
x = y

The cost of papering the wall is:
cost = length * cost per meter
length = sum of the lengths of the other two sides multiplied by the height of the room.
length = (5y/2 - x + 5y/2 + x) * 2x
length = 10yx

Area of the wall = length * height = 20xy^2

Area to be papered = Area of the wall - Area of doors and windows
Area to be papered = 20xy^2 - 15

Cost of papering = Area to be papered * cost per meter
260 = (20xy^2 - 15) * (2/100)
1300 = 20xy^2 - 15
20xy^2 = 1315

Substituting x = y, we get:
20x^3 = 1315
x^3 = 65.75
x = 4.2

Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 8.4 meters.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 44 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man walks at 5 kmph for 6 hrs and at 4 kmph for 12 hrs. His average speed is
Choices:
  A: 4 1/3 km/h
  B: 7 2/3 km/h
  C: 9 ½ km/h
  D: 8 km/h
  E: 81 km/h
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can use the formula of average speed = total distance / total time to find the average speed.
  Let's find the total distance first.
  Distance traveled in the first 6 hours = 5 kmph x 6 hrs = 30 km
  Distance traveled in the next 12 hours = 4 kmph x 12 hrs = 48 km
  Total distance traveled = 30 km + 48 km = 78 km
  Total time taken = 6 hrs + 12 hrs = 18 hrs
  Average speed = total distance / total time = 78 km / 18 hrs = 13/3 km/h = 4 1/3 km/h
  Therefore, the answer is A: 4 1/3 km/h
Action: Answer("A")

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 46 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The difference between the squares of two numbers is 256000 and the sum of the numbers is 1000. The numbers are
Choices:
  A: 600, 400
  B: 628, 372
  C: 640, 360
  D: None of these
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's use algebra to solve the problem.
  Let's assume that the two numbers are x and y.
  According to the problem, we have two equations:
  x^2 - y^2 = 256000
  x + y = 1000
  We can factor x^2 - y^2 as (x+y)(x-y), so we have:
  (x+y)(x-y) = 256000
  x+y = 1000
  We can substitute x+y with 1000, and we get:
  (1000)(x-y) = 256000
  x-y = 256
  Now we have two equations:
  x+y = 1000
  x-y = 256
  We can solve for x by adding the two equations:
  2x = 1256
  x = 628
  We can substitute x with 628 in one of the equations to find y:
  x+y = 1000
  628+y = 1000
  y = 372
  Therefore, the two numbers are 628 and 372.
  The answer is B: 628, 372.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume x and y are the two numbers. 
  The given information can be written as:
    x^2 - y^2 = 256000
    x + y = 1000
  We can use the second equation to solve for one of the variables in terms of the other.
    x = 1000 - y
  We can substitute this expression for x into the first equation.
    (1000 - y)^2 - y^2 = 256000
    1000000 - 2000y + y^2 - y^2 = 256000
    1000000 - 2000y = 256000
    2000y = 744000
    y = 372
  Now that we know y, we can use the second equation to solve for x.
    x + 372 = 1000
    x = 628
  Therefore, the two numbers are 628 and 372.
  The answer is B: 628, 372.

  y = 372

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 47 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month, at a production cost to the company of $110 per component, and sells all of the components by the end of each month. What is the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) will be at least $626,400 ?
Choices:
  A: 226
  B: 230
  C: 240
  D: 260
  E: 280
Response 0:
Thought:
  The company produces 420 units of a computer component every month.
  The production cost of each component is $110.
  Therefore, the total production cost per month is 420 x $110 = $46,200.
  The yearly production cost is $46,200 x 12 = $554,400.
  The yearly profit should be at least $626,400, which is the sum of the yearly production cost and profit.
  Therefore, the minimum yearly profit is $626,400 - $554,400 = $72,000.
  The company sells 420 units every month, so it sells 420 x 12 = 5,040 units every year.
  Let's assume that the minimum selling price per component is x.
  Then the yearly revenue is 5,040x.
  The yearly profit is the yearly revenue minus the yearly production cost, which is 5,040x - $554,400.
  We need to find the value of x that satisfies the equation 5,040x - $554,400 >= $72,000.
  Solving for x in this inequality gives x >= $146.67.
  Therefore, the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit will be at least $626,400 is $147 or more.
  The answer is not one of the given choices.
  None of the above.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The yearly production of components is 420 * 12 = 5040.
  The production cost of each component is $110.
  Therefore, the total production cost of 5040 components is $110 * 5040 = $554,400.
  The yearly profit should be at least $626,400 - $554,400 = $72,000.

Question: A starts travel towards south 3km, then travel 5 km towards east, and again travels 3 km to north, and finally travels 2km towards west. In the end how far from is A from home?
Choices:
  A: 3km
  B: 2km
  C: 4km
  D: 5km
  E: 6km
Response 0:
Thought:
  A starts at some point and ends up at some other point after traveling south, east, north, and west.
  A's initial and final location is the same point (home).
  A moves 3km south and 3km north, which cancels out.
  A moves 5km east and 2km west, which results in a net movement of 3km east.
  Therefore, A is 3km away from home in the east direction.
  The answer is A: 3km.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  A travels 3 km towards south and then 3 km towards north. This means A is back to the starting point, so the net displacement in the north-south direction is zero.
  A travels 5 km towards east and then 2 km towards west. This means the net displacement in the east-west direction is 5 - 2 = 3 km towards east.
  A is 3 km east from home.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Thought:
  A can be visualized as moving in a square, where the first and last legs of the square cancel each other out.
  The second and third legs of the square form a right triangle with legs 5km and 3km respectively.
  The hypotenuse of this right triangle is the distance between A's final position and the starting position.
  Therefore, we can use the Pythagorean theorem to solve for the hypotenuse.
  a^2 + b^2 = c^2, where a = 5km and b = 3km.
  c^2 = 5^2 + 3^2 = 34
  c = sqrt(34) km
  The answer is approximately 5.83 km.
  Rounding to the nearest km, the answer is 6km.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 51 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What should come in place of the question mark(?) in each of the following questions ?
a2 - b2/(a + b)2 (?)=(a - b)2
Choices:
  A: (a + b)(a - b)
  B: (a - b)2
  C: (a + b)2
  D: a3 + b3
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can use the identity a2 - b2 = (a-b)(a+b)
  Substituting this identity in the given equation we get,
  [(a-b)(a+b)]/[(a+b)2] = (a-b)2
  Cancelling (a-b) from both sides, we get:
  (a+b)/(a+b) = (a-b)
  Therefore, the answer is (a-b).
  The answer is B: (a - b)2.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We will use the formula a^2 - b^2 = (a + b)(a - b) to solve the question.
  Given equation: a^2 - b^2 / (a + b)^2 = (a - b)^2
  LHS = a^2 - b^2 / (a + b)^2
  = (a + b)(a - b) / (a + b)^2
  = (a - b) / (a + b)
  Now, we compare LHS and RHS:
  LHS = (a - b) / (a + b) = RHS = (a - b)^2 / (a + b)^2
  Taking square roots on both sides, we get:
  a - b / a + b = (a - b) / (a + b)
  a - b = a - b
  Therefore, the missing term is (a + b).
  The answer is A: (a + b)(a - b).
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:

    (q - p) * x = $1500 * n - $3000 * x
    (q - p + $3000) * x = $1500 * n
    x = ($1500 * n) / (q - p + $3000)
  We know that x is an integer, so ($1500 * n) % (q - p + $3000) = 0.
  We can try different values of n and see which one satisfies this condition.
  Let's start with n = 2.
  If there are only two family members, then x = 1 and n/2 - x = 1.
  The equation becomes:
    (q - p) * 1 = $3000 * 1
    q - p = $3000
  We also know that the total income is $9000:
    p + q = $9000
  Solving these equations, we get p = $3000 and q = $6000.
  Therefore, there are two family members, and one of them earns $3000 and the other earns $6000.
  This does not satisfy the condition that ($1500 * n) % (q - p + $3000) = 0, so we need to try a larger value of n.
  Let's try n = 4.
  If there are four family members, then x = 2 and n/2 - x = 0.
  The equation becomes:
    (q - p) * 2 = $3000 * 2
    q - p = $3000
  We also know that the total income is $9000:
    2 * p + 2 * q = $9000
    p + q = $4500
  Solving these equations, we get p = $1500 and q = $4500.
  Therefore, there are four family members, and two of them earn $1500 and the other two earn $4500.
  This satisfies the condition that ($1500 * n) % (q - p + $3000) = 0.
  So, the answer is C: 4.

Question: A starts a business with Rs.40,000. After 2 months, B joined him with Rs.60,000. C joined them after some more time with Rs.120,000. At the end of the year, out of a total profit of Rs.375,000, C gets Rs.150,000 as his share. How many months after B joined the business, did C join?
Choices:
  A: 2 months
  B: 4 months
  C: 23 months
  D: 24 months
  E: 84 months
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that C joined the business after x months.
  Hence, A invested for 12 months, B invested for (12-2)=10 months, and C invested for (12-x) months.
  The ratio of their investments is 4:6:12, which can be simplified to 2:3:6.
  Let's calculate the total profit share of A and B.
  Let A's share be 2k, B's share be 3k, and C's share be 6k.
  Total profit = 2k + 3k + 6k = 11k
  C's share = Rs.150,000
  Hence, 6k = Rs.150,000
  Therefore, k = Rs.25,000
  A's share = 2k = Rs.50,000
  B's share = 3k = Rs.75,000
  A's profit = (40,000/100,000) * 50,000 = Rs.20,000
  B's profit = (60,000/100,000) * 75,000 = Rs.45,000
  Total profit until C joined = 20,000 + 45,000 = Rs.65,000
  Profit earned after C joined = 375,000 - 65,000 = Rs.310,000
  C's profit = (120,000/220,000) * 310,000 = Rs.168,181.82
  C's share = Rs.150,000
  This means that C had to return Rs.18,181.82 to the business.
  Let's assume that C joined after m months.
  Hence, B invested for m-x months.
  B's profit = (60,000/100,000) * 75,000 = Rs.45,000
  C's profit = (120,000/220,000) * (310,000-45,000) = Rs.147,272.73
  C returned Rs.18,181.82 to the business, so his actual profit was Rs.168,181.82 - Rs.18,181.82 = Rs.150,000
  (120,000/220,000) * (310,000-45,000) - 18,181.82 = 150,000
  (120,000/220,000) * 265,000 = 168,181.82
  120,000 * 265,000 = 220,000 * 168,181.82
  x = (220,000 * 168,181.82 - 120,000 * 265,000) / (120,000 - 220,000)
  x = 23.0769 months
  Therefore, C joined the business after 23 months (rounded off to the nearest month).
  The answer is C: 23 months.

Question: The monthly salary S of a shop assistant is the sum of a fixed salary of $500 plus 5% of all monthly sales. What should the monthly sales be so that her monthly salary reaches $1500?
Choices:
  A: $50000
  B: $40000
  C: $30000
  D: $20000
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  The monthly salary S of the shop assistant is $1500.
  The fixed salary of the shop assistant is $500.
  The monthly sales is x.
  The monthly salary S is the sum of the fixed salary and 5% of monthly sales, so S = 500 + 0.05x.
  We need to find the monthly sales x that will make the monthly salary S equal to $1500.
  We can set up an equation to solve for x: 1500 = 500 + 0.05x
  Subtract 500 from both sides: 1000 = 0.05x
  Divide both sides by 0.05: x = 20000
  Therefore, the monthly sales should be $20000.
Action: Answer("D")

Question: The sum of k consecutive integers is 51. If the least integer is -50, then k =
Choices:
  A: 40
  B: 62
  C: 82
  D: 92
  E: 102
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's call the first integer x.
  Since there are k consecutive integers, the sum of the k integers can be expressed as x + (x+1) + (x+2) + ... + (x+k-1)
  We know that the least integer is -50, so x = -50.
  Substituting -50 for x, we get -50 + (-49) + (-48) + ... + (x+k-1) = 51.
  Simplifying the equation, we get (-50)*k + (1+2+3+...+k) = 51.
  We know that 1+2+3+...+k = k*(k+1)/2, so we can substitute to get (-50)*k + k*(k+1)/2 = 51.
  Multiplying both sides by 2 to get rid of the fraction, we get -100k + k*(k+1) = 102.
  Simplifying the equation, we get k^2 - 99k + 102 = 0.
  Using the quadratic formula, we get k = (99 ± sqrt(99^2 - 4*1*102))/2
  k is positive, so we take the positive solution, which is k = (99 + sqrt(9405))/2.
  This is approximately equal to 62.9, so the closest integer value to k is 63.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 62.

Question: A certain liquid passes through a drain at a rate of w/25 gallons every x seconds. At that rate, how many minutes will it take y gallons to pass through the drain?
Choices:
  A: y/(1200xy)
  B: 20xy/w
  C: 5xy/(12w)
  D: w/(3xy)
  E: 3y/(wx)
Response 0:
Thought:
  The rate at which the liquid passes through the drain is w/25 gallons per x seconds.
  The number of gallons that pass through the drain in t seconds is (w/25) * (t/x).
  If we want to know how long it will take y gallons to pass through the drain, we can set (w/25) * (t/x) = y and solve for t.
  Multiplying both sides by (25x/w), we get t = (25xy/w).
  To convert t to minutes, we divide by 60.
  Therefore, t in minutes is t/60 = (25xy)/(60w).
  Simplifying this expression gives t/60 = (5xy)/(12w).
  Therefore, the answer is C: 5xy/(12w).
Action: Answer("C")

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 60 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A square piece of cloth is trimmed by 4 feet on one edge to form a rectangular piece, which is then cut diagonally in half to create two triangles. If the area of each of triangle is 70 square feet, what was the perimeter (in feet) of the original piece of square cloth?
Choices:
  A: 56
  B: 58
  C: 60
  D: 62
  E: 64
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the original square piece of cloth had sides of length x feet.
  After trimming 4 feet from one edge, the rectangular piece has dimensions x-4 by x feet.
  The area of the rectangle is (x-4)x = x^2 - 4x square feet.
  Cutting the rectangle diagonally in half creates two congruent right triangles.
  The area of each triangle is 70 square feet, so the area of the rectangle is 2(70) = 140 square feet.
  Therefore, x^2 - 4x = 140.
  Rearranging this equation gives x^2 - 4x - 140 = 0.
  Factoring this quadratic equation gives (x-14)(x+10) = 0.
  Since x must be positive, we have x = 14.
  Therefore, the original square piece of cloth had sides of length 14 feet.
  The perimeter of the original piece of cloth is 4x = 56 feet.
  The answer is A: 56.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:

  The base and height of each triangle are x-4 and (x-4)/2 respectively.
  Therefore, (1/2) * (x-4) * (x-4)/2 = 70.
  Solving the equation gives x = 14.
  The perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4x.
  Therefore, the perimeter is 4 * 14 = 56.
  The answer is A: 56.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 61 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular parking space is marked out by painting three of its sides. If the length of the unpainted side is 9 feet, and the sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, then what is the area of the parking space in square feet?
Choices:
  A: 46
  B: 81
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: None
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's call the width of the parking space as w and the length as l.
  We know that one side (width) is unpainted and its length is 9 feet.
  The sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, so we have:
  l + 2w = 37
  We can rearrange the above equation to solve for l:
  l = 37 - 2w
  The area of a rectangle is given by the formula A = lw.
  Substituting l = 37 - 2w and w = 9, we get:
  A = (37 - 2(9)) × 9
  A = 19 × 9
  A = 171 square feet.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 46.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's represent the length of the painted sides as l and w.
  We know that l + w + l = 37, which simplifies to 2l + w = 37.
  We also know that w = 9.
  Solving for l, we have 2l = 28, which gives us l = 14.
  Therefore, the area of the rectangle is l x w = 14 x 9 = 126.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let's represent the length of the painted sides as x and y.
  We know that x + y + 9 = 37.
  Therefore, x + y = 28.
  The area of a rectangle is length times width.
  We know that the width is 9 feet.
  We can represent the length as l.
  Therefore, the area of the parking space is l * 9.
  We also know that x + y = 28.
  We can represent the area as x * y.
  We can use the formula (x + y)^2 = x^2 + 2xy + y^2 to solve for xy.
  (x + y)^2 = x^2 + 2xy + y^2
  28^2 = x^2 + 2xy + y^2
  784 = x^2 + 2xy + y^2
  784 = (x+y)^2 - 2xy
  784 = 28^2 - 2xy
  784 = 784 - 2xy
  2xy = 0
  xy = 0
  Therefore, the area of the parking space is 0 square feet.
  The answer is E: None.
Action: Answer("E")

Thought:
  Let's assume the length of the painted sides is "L" and the width is "W".
  We are given that the length of the unpainted side is 9 feet.
  The sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet.
  Therefore, L + W + L = 37, which simplifies to 2L + W = 37.
  We need to find the area of the parking space, which is given by A = LW.
  We can use the equation 2L + W = 37 to solve for W in terms of L.
  W = 37 - 2L.
  Substituting W with 37 - 2L in the equation A = LW, we get A = L(37 - 2L) = 37L - 2L^2.
  To maximize the area, we can take the derivative of A with respect to L and set it equal to zero.
  dA/dL = 37 - 4L = 0, which implies L = 37/4.
  Plugging L = 37/4 into the equation A = 37L - 2L^2, we get A = 81.25.
  Therefore, the area of the parking space in square feet is 81.25.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 63 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Hoses A and B spout water at different constant rates, and hose A can fill a certain pool in 8 hours. Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours and the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours. How many hours would it have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool?
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 15
  C: 12
  D: 6
  E: 3
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's assume that hose A can fill the pool in x hours.
Then, its rate is 1/x of the pool per hour.
Since it takes 8 hours for hose A to fill the pool, the fraction of the pool filled by hose A in 1 hour is 1/8.
Let's assume that hose B can fill the pool in y hours.
Then, its rate is 1/y of the pool per hour.
In the first 2 hours, hose A fills 2/8 = 1/4 of the pool.
In the next 3 hours, both hoses fill 3*(1/x + 1/y) = 3/x + 3/y of the pool.
Since the pool is completely filled in these 5 hours, we can set up the equation:
1/4 + 3/x + 3/y = 1
Simplifying the equation, we get:
3/x + 3/y = 3/4
1/x + 1/y = 1/4
Multiplying both sides by xy, we get:
y + x = xy/4
xy - 4y - 4x = 0
(xy - 4y) - 4x = 0
y(x - 4) = 4x
y = 4x/(x - 4)
Since y is the time it would take hose B to fill the pool alone, we need to find y when x = 8.
y = 4*8/(8 - 4) = 12
Therefore, hose B, working alone, would take 12 hours to fill the entire pool.
The answer is C: 12.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume that hose A can fill the pool in x hours.
  Therefore, the rate at which hose A can fill the pool is 1/x.
  Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours, so the amount of water filled by hose A in the first 2 hours is 2/x.
  The two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours, so the amount of water filled by both hoses in the next 3 hours is 3*(1/x + 1/y), where y is the rate at which hose B can fill the pool.
  The total amount of water filled by both hoses is 1, so we can set up the equation as follows:
  2/x + 3*(1/x + 1/y) = 1
  Solving for y, we get:
  y = 15x
  This means that hose B can fill the pool in 15 hours.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 15.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:

  Let rB be the rate at which hose B fills the pool.
  The amount of work done is equal to the rate multiplied by the time.
  Therefore, the amount of work done by hose A in the first 2 hours is 2rA.
  The amount of work left to do is 1 - (2rA / rA) = 1/4 of the whole job.
  The amount of work done by both hoses in the next 3 hours is (3/5) * (rA + rB).
  The amount of work done by hose B in the same 3 hours is (3/5) * rB.
  Equating the amount of work done by both hoses and hose B alone, we get:
  (3/5) * (rA + rB) = 1/4
  (3/5) * rB = 1/4 - 3/5 * rA
  Solving for rA, we get rA = 1/40.
  Substituting rA in the second equation and solving for rB, we get rB = 1/24.
  Therefore, hose B can fill the pool alone in 24 hours.
  The answer is D: 6.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 64 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Two numbers are in the ratio 3:5. If 9 is subtracted from each, the new numbers are in the ratio 12:23. The smaller number is?
Choices:
  A: 21
  B: 33
  C: 35
  D: 42
  E: 58
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the two numbers in the ratio 3:5 are 3x and 5x respectively.
  If 9 is subtracted from each of them, the two numbers become 3x - 9 and 5x - 9.
  The new ratio is 12:23, which means (3x - 9) is to (5x - 9) as 12 is to 23.
  We can set up an equation to solve for x and then find the value of the smaller number, which is 3x.
  3x - 9 : 5x - 9 = 12 : 23
  Cross-multiplying, we get: (3x - 9) × 23 = (5x - 9) × 12
  Solving for x, we get x = 33
  Therefore, the smaller number is 3x = 99.
  The answer is B: 33.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:

  Cross-multiplying, we get:
  69x - 207 = 60x - 108
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = 27
  Therefore, the smaller number is 3x - 9 = 72.
  The answer is not in the choices, so the most likely answer is D: 42.

Choices:

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 66 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In a large forest, 300 deer were caught, tagged, and returned during 2001. During 2002, 500 deer were caught at random, of which only 20 had tags from the previous year. If the percent of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year and were caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags, what is the total deer population in the forest (assuming no change in population between 2001 and 2002)?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 500
  C: 5000
  D: 6000
  E: 7500
Response 0:
Thought:
- In 2001, 300 deer were caught, tagged, and released.
- In 2002, 500 deer were caught, and 20 of them had tags from the previous year.
- We assume that the percentage of tagged deer in the sample is the same as the percentage of tagged deer in the entire population.
- Let's use "x" to represent the total number of deer in the forest.
- The percentage of tagged deer in the sample is 20/500 = 4%.
- We can set up an equation using this information: 4% of x = 300.
- Solving for x, we get x = 7,500.
- Therefore, the total deer population in the forest is 7,500.
- The answer is E: 7500.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let D be the total deer population. 
In 2001, 300 deer were tagged, so the proportion of deer tagged is 300/D. 
In 2002, 20 of the 500 deer caught had tags from 2001, so the proportion of deer tagged is 20/500. 
Since the proportion of tagged deer in the sample of 500 is representative of the total population, we can set up an equation: 

300/D = 20/500 

To solve for D, we can cross-multiply and simplify: 

20D = 300 * 500 

D = 7500 

Therefore, the total deer population in the forest is 7500.

Question: In an exam, a candidate secured 504 marks of the maximum mark of M. If the maximum mark M is converted into 800 marks, he would have secured 420 marks. What is the value of M?
Choices:
  A: 278
  B: 2890
  C: 270
  D: 2702
  E: 960
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's use proportionality to solve this problem.
  If the candidate secured 504 marks out of M maximum marks, then his percentage score is 504/M.
  If the same candidate secured 420 marks out of 800 maximum marks, then his percentage score is 420/800.
  We can set up a proportion and solve for M.
  504/M = 420/800
  Cross-multiplying, we get 504*800 = 420*M
  Simplifying, we get M = (504*800)/420 = 960
  Therefore, the value of M is 960.
Action: Answer("E")
