### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 68 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: On dividing 2272 and 875 by a 3-digit number N, we get the same remainder. The sum of the digits of N is:
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 11
  C: 12
  D: 13
  E: 14
Response 0:
Thought:
  When we divide two numbers by the same 3-digit number N, we get the same remainder, which means the difference between the two numbers is divisible by N.
  Let's call the remainder R.
  We have:
  2272 = kN + R
  875 = mN + R
  where k and m are integers.
  Subtracting the second equation from the first, we get:
  1397 = (k - m)N
  Since N is a 3-digit number, we know that N >= 100 and N <= 999.
  Therefore, k - m must be a factor of 1397.
  The prime factors of 1397 are 1397 and 1, which means k - m can only be 1 or 1397.
  If k - m = 1, then N = 1397, which is not a 3-digit number, so this is not possible.
  Therefore, k - m = 1397, which means N = 1397/7 = 199.
  The sum of the digits of N is 1 + 9 + 9 = 19.
  The answer is not among the choices. However, the most likely answer is E: 14.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought: 
To get the same remainder when dividing 2272 and 875 by N, we need to find the HCF of the differences between the two numbers, i.e., (2272 - 875) = 1397.
Prime factorizing 1397, we get 1397 = 19 × 73.
Thus, N must be a factor of 1397.
The sum of the digits of 1397 is 20, which is not in the choices.
The sum of the digits of 19 and 73 is 10 and 10, respectively.
Therefore, the sum of the digits of N is 10.
The answer is A: 10.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
Let's use the concept of the remainder theorem.
If a number P is divided by N, then the remainder will be equal to P-N*(P//N), where // denotes the floor division operator.
Let's assume that the common remainder is R.
So, we have:
  2272 = N * Q1 + R
  875 = N * Q2 + R
Subtracting the 2 equations, we get:
  1397 = N * (Q1 - Q2)
Since N is a 3-digit number, it can be written as N = 100a + 10b + c, where a, b, and c are single-digit numbers.
The sum of the digits of N is a + b + c.
Let's find the possible values of a, b, and c.
Since N is a factor of 1397, we have:
  1397 = N * (Q1 - Q2)
  1397 = (100a + 10b + c) * (Q1 - Q2)
  1397 = 100aQ1 - 100aQ2 + 10bQ1 - 10bQ2 + cQ1 - cQ2
  1397 = (100aQ1 - 100aQ2) + (10bQ1 - 10bQ2) + (cQ1 - cQ2)
  1397 = 100(aQ1 - aQ2) + 10(bQ1 - bQ2) + (cQ1 - cQ2)
Since N is a 3-digit number, we have 100 <= N <= 999, which implies 1 <= a <= 9.
Let's consider all the possible values of a and find the corresponding values of b and c.
For a = 1, we have:
  1397 = 100(Q1 - Q2) + 10(bQ1 - bQ2) + (cQ1 - cQ2)
  1397 = 100(Q1 - Q2) + 10(bQ1 - bQ2) + (cQ1 - cQ2)
  1397 = 100(Q1 - Q2) + 10(bQ1 - bQ2) + (cQ1 - cQ2)

Question: By himself, Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours. On a particular day, he happens to finish two-thirds of the work. The remaining portion of the work is done by Jill, whose rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do. How long does it take Jill to finish the remaining work?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 8
  C: 22
  D: 50
  E: 20
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours.
  Jack finished two-thirds of the work.
  So, the remaining one-third of the work is done by Jill.
  Jill's rate of cleaning is 5% of what Jack can do.
  Let's assume that Jill can clean the remaining one-third of the yacht in x hours.
  Jack's rate of cleaning is 1 yacht per 12 hours, which is 1/12 yacht per hour.
  Jill's rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do, so her rate of cleaning is 5/100 * 1/12 = 1/240 yacht per hour.
  Jack did two-thirds of the work, which means he cleaned 2/3 of a yacht.
  The remaining one-third of the work is done by Jill, which means she cleaned 1/3 of a yacht.
  We know that the amount of work done is equal to the rate of cleaning multiplied by the time taken to do the work.
  So, we can set up the equation: 1/12 * (2/3) + 1/240 * x = 1/3.
  Solving for x, we get x = 20.
  Therefore, it takes Jill 20 hours to finish the remaining work.
  The answer is E: 20.

Question: Mr.Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train. How long would he have taken if he had traveled by car in both ways?
Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the time taken by Mr. Sam to travel to the city is "t1" and the time taken to return from the city is "t2".
  From the problem, we know that t1 + t2 = 17.
  We also know that 2t1 - 4 = t1 + t2.
  Solving these equations, we get t1 = 7 and t2 = 10.
  If he had traveled by car in both ways, the total time taken would be t1 + t2 = 7 + 10 = 17 hours.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 20 hrs.
Action: Answer("D")

  20c + 325 = 340
  20c = 15
  c = 15/20
  c = 3/4
  The minimum number of copper coins that she brought is 3.

Question: The sum of the digits of a three digit number is 17, and the sum of the squares of its digits is 109. If we subtract 495 from the number, we shall get a number consisting of the same digits written in the reverse order. Find the number.
Choices:
  A: 368
  B: 377
  C: 288
  D: 997
  E: 112
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the three-digit number is `abc`.
  We know that `a+b+c=17`.
  We also know that `a^2+b^2+c^2=109`.
  We know that after subtracting 495 from the number, the digits will be in reverse order.
  This implies that `a=c`.
  Let's substitute `c` with `a` in the above equations.
  Therefore, `2a+b=17` and `2a^2 + b^2 = 109`.
  We can now use trial and error to get the answer.

Trial and error:
  We can start by trying `a=6` and `b=5`, then `a=7` and `b=3`.
  If we substitute `a=6` and `b=5`, we get `c=6`, which means the original number is `656`.
  After subtracting `495` from `656`, we get `161`.
  The digits of `161` are not in reverse order, so this is not the answer.
  If we substitute `a=7` and `b=3`, we get `c=7`, which means the original number is `737`.
  After subtracting `495` from `737`, we get `242`.
  The digits of `242` are in reverse order, so this is the answer.

Therefore, the answer is D: 997.

Topic: Math
Question: The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is?
Choices:
  A: 2: π
  B: 7:2
  C: 8:2
  D: 6: π
  E: 8:3
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the side of the cube is "a". Therefore, the volume of the cube will be a^3.
  The diameter of the sphere will be equal to the edge of the cube, which is "a".
  The radius of the sphere will be half of the diameter and will be equal to "a/2".
  The volume of the sphere will be (4/3)π (a/2)^3.
  The ratio of the volume of the cube to the sphere will be a^3 : (4/3)π (a/2)^3.
  We can simplify this ratio to 6:π.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 6:π.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let the edge of the cube be 'a'
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the edge of the cube 'a'
  The radius of the sphere is equal to a/2
  The volume of the sphere is (4/3)π(r^3) = (4/3)π(a/2)^3 = (1/6)πa^3
  The volume of the cube is a^3
  The ratio of the volume of the cube to that of the sphere is (a^3)/[(1/6)πa^3] = (6/π)
  Therefore, the answer is D: 6:π

  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the side of the cube.
  Therefore, d = 2r = a.
  The volume of the cube is Vc = a^3.
  The volume of the sphere is Vs = (4/3)πr^3 = (4/3)π(a/2)^3 = (1/6)πa^3.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is Vc:Vs = a^3:(1/6)πa^3 = 6:(π).
  Therefore, the answer is A: 6:π.
Action: Answer("A")

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 75 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: There are ten lime soda bottles on a table in a restaurant. They are to be served among two different groups of customers consisting of 5 members each. How many ways are there to create these 2 groups?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 105
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: 525
Response 0:
Thought:
  There are 10 bottles of lime soda to be divided into two groups.
  The first group can have any combination of 5 bottles selected from the 10.
  The second group will then consist of the remaining 5 bottles.
  The order in which the groups are selected does not matter.
  The formula for selecting r items from n items is nCr = n! / r!(n-r)!
  Therefore, the answer is 10C5 = 10! / 5!(10-5)! = 252.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We need to divide 10 bottles into two groups of 5 each.
  The first group can be chosen in 10 choose 5 ways.
  The second group will be the remaining bottles.
  Therefore, the second group can be chosen in 5 choose 5 = 1 way.
  The total number of ways to divide the bottles is the product of the number of ways to choose the two groups.
  Therefore, the answer is 10 choose 5 * 5 choose 5 = 252.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  We have 10 lime soda bottles to be served.
  There are 2 groups of customers consisting of 5 members each.
  The number of ways to choose 5 bottles out of 10 is 10! / (5! * (10-5)!) = 252.
  We divide this number by 2! because we don't care about the order of the two groups.
  Therefore, the number of ways to create these 2 groups is 252 / 2 = 126.

  5 choose 5 is 1

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 76 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's use the formula n(A U B) = n(A) + n(B) - n(A and B), where n(A) is the number of files infected by a virus, n(B) is the number of files infected by a worm, and n(A and B) is the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  Then, we know that:
  n(A U B) = 250 (since all files are either infected by a virus or a worm or both)
  n(A and B) = x (where x is a positive integer)
  n(B only) = 2.5x
  n(A only) = 0.5(250 - x)
  We want to find the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm, which is:
  250 - n(B) - n(A and B)
  Now we need to solve for x to find n(B) and n(A and B).
Action: Answer("C") 75. 

Solution:
  n(A only) = 0.5(250 - x) = 125 - 0.5x
  n(B only) = 2.5x
  n(A and B) = x
  n(A U B) = n(A) + n(B) - n(A and B)
            = (125 - 0.5x) + 2.5x - x
            = 125 + 1.5x
  250 = 125 + 1.5x
  1.5x = 125
  x = 83.33
  Since x must be a positive integer, we round up to x = 84.
  n(B) = n(B only) + n(A and B) = 2.5x + x = 3.5x = 294
  n(not B) = 250 - n(B) - n(A and B) = 250 - 294 - 84 = -128
  Since the number of files that are not infected by a worm cannot be negative, we know that there is an error in our calculations. However, we can still find the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm by subtracting the number of files that were infected by a worm from the total number of files:
  n(not B) = 250 - n(B only) = 250 - 2.5x = 250 - 2.5(84) = 58.
  Therefore, 58 of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm. Answer("C") is correct.
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let V be the set of files infected by a virus, W be the set of files infected by a worm, and VW be the set of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  We know that |V ∪ W| = 250, where ∪ denotes union.
  We also know that |W \ VW| = 2.5 |VW|.
  We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, so |Vc| = 0.5 |V ∪ W|, where c denotes complement.
  We want to find |Wc|.
  We can use the Principle of Inclusion-Exclusion (PIE) to solve for |Wc|.
  PIE states that |V ∪ W| = |V| + |W| - |V ∩ W|.
  Rearranging this equation and using the given information yields:
    |V ∩ W| = (|V| + |W| + |VW|)/2 = (0.5 |V ∪ W| + |VW|)/2 = (250 - |Vc| + |VW|)/2.
    |W| = |W \ VW| + |VW| = 3.5 |VW|.
    |V ∪ Wc| = |Vc| + |Wc \ VW| = |Vc| + |Wc| - |VW|.
  Substituting the above equations into the PIE equation yields:
    250 = 1.5 |V ∪ W| + 2.5 |VW| + |Vc| + |Wc|.
  Solving for |Wc| yields:
    |Wc| = 250 - 1.5 |V ∪ W| - 2.5 |VW| - |Vc|.
    Substituting the known values yields:
    |Wc| = 90.
  Therefore, the answer is E: 125.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 77 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A trader sold an article at a profit of 20% for Rs.360. What is the cost price of the article?
Choices:
  A: 270
  B: 300
  C: 280
  D: 320
  E: 315
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let CP be the cost price of the article.
  Profit% = 20%
  Selling price = Rs.360
  We know that, Selling price (SP) = Cost price (CP) + Profit (P)
  Profit% = (P/CP) × 100
  (P/CP) × 100 = 20%
  P = 0.2CP
  SP = CP + 0.2CP = 1.2CP
  1.2CP = 360
  CP = 360/1.2 = Rs.300
  Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs.300.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume the cost price of the article is "x".
  The trader sold the article at a profit of 20%, which means the selling price is 120% of the cost price.
  We can write the equation as: 120% of x = Rs.360
  We know that 120% is the same as 1.2.
  So, the equation can be written as: 1.2x = 360
  Solving for x, we get: x = 360/1.2 = 300
  Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs.300.
  The answer is B: 300.
Action: Answer("B")

  CP = (SP * 100) / (100 + P)
  where CP is the cost price, SP is the selling price, and P is the percentage profit.
  We know the selling price is Rs.360 and the percentage profit is 20%.
  Therefore, the cost price is (360 * 100) / (100 + 20) = 300.
  The cost price of the article is Rs.300.

So, 1.2x = 360
Solving the above equation, we get x = 300.
Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs.300.

Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Thought:
- Let's call the number of newspapers bought on Sunday "x", and the number of newspapers bought every other day of the week "y".
- We know that the hotel buys twice as many newspapers on Sunday as it does on any other day of the week. Therefore, x = 2y.
- We also know that the hotel pays $4 for every Sunday newspaper, and $1 for every newspaper bought on any other day of the week. Therefore, the total cost per week is 4x + 1(7y) = 210.
- Substituting x = 2y into the equation above, we get 4(2y) + 7y = 210.
- Solving for y, we get y = 15.
- Therefore, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on Monday. 
- Answer: A: 15.

Action: Answer("A")

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###

Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's call the distance between X and Y as D.
  Let's call the time taken by both Allen and Bob to meet for the first time as T.
  Let's call the time taken by Allen to reach Y as T1.
  Let's call the distance travelled by Allen from X to Y as D1.
  Let's call the distance travelled by Bob from Y to X as D2.
  Distance travelled by Allen in T1 = D1
  Distance travelled by Bob in T1 = D - D2
  Distance travelled by Allen in T = 54T
  Distance travelled by Bob in T = 78T
  Distance travelled by Allen in returning from Y to X = D1
  Distance travelled by Bob in returning from X to Y = D2
  We know that they meet at the midpoint of their journey for the second time.
  Therefore, distance travelled by Allen in returning from Y to X = Distance travelled by Bob in returning from X to Y.
  We also know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time.
  Therefore, D2 - D1 = 48
  We can now write equations for D1 and D2 in terms of T and D.
  D1 = 54T1
  D2 = 78(T - T1)
  Adding the above two equations, we get:
  D = D1 + D2 = 54T1 + 78(T - T1)
  Simplifying the above equation, we get:
  D = 24T1 + 78T
  We also know that D2 - D1 = 48
  Substituting the values of D1 and D2 in the above equation, we get:
  78(T - T1) - 54T1 = 48
  Simplifying the above equation, we get:
  T = 6 hours
  Substituting the value of T in the equation D = 24T1 + 78T, we get:
  D = 504 km
  The distance between X and Y is 504/2 = 252 km.
  Therefore, the answer is not in the choices.
Response 1:
Thought:
Let the distance between X and Y be d.
Let t be the time taken for Allen and Bob to meet for the second time.
Let the distance Allen travels from X to Y be x.
Let the distance Bob travels from Y to X be y.
Total distance travelled by Allen = x + (d - x) + (d - x) = 2d
Total distance travelled by Bob = y + (d - y) + (d - y) = 2d
Since Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78 kmph, we can say:
x/54 = (d - y)/78  ---- (1)
(d - y)/54 = y/78  ---- (2)
Solving equations (1) and (2), we get:
y = 2d/5
x = 3d/5
We are given that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen when they meet for the second time. 
So, y - x = 48
Substituting the values of x and y, we get:
2d/5 - 3d/5 = 48
Solving for d, we get:
d = 120 km
Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 120 km.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 81 of 100 ###

Question: A jeep travels a certain distance taking 6 hours in the forward journey. During the return journey, it increased its speed by 12km/hr and took 4 hours. What is the distance travelled by the jeep?
Choices:
  A: 126km
  B: 144km
  C: 127km
  D: 228km
  E: 128km
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the speed during the forward journey be S.
  Let the distance travelled be D.
  Time taken during forward journey = 6 hours.
  Time taken during the return journey = 4 hours.
  Speed during the return journey = S + 12 km/hr.
  We know that distance = speed x time.
  Therefore, D = S x 6 (distance during forward journey)
  D = (S + 12) x 4 (distance during return journey)
  Equating both equations, we get 6S = 4(S + 12)
  Solving this equation, we get S = 18km/hr.
  Therefore, D = 6 x 18 = 108km
  The answer is 108km.

  Let the speed of the jeep during the forward journey be "s".
  During the return journey, the speed of the jeep is increased to "s+12".
  We know that distance = speed × time.
  From the information given in the question, we can form two equations:
    d = 6s   (since the forward journey took 6 hours)
    d = 4(s+12)  (since the return journey took 4 hours and the speed increased by 12km/hr)
  Substituting the first equation into the second equation, we get:
    6s = 4(s+12)
    6s = 4s + 48
    2s = 48
    s = 24
  Substituting s = 24 into the first equation, we get:
    d = 6s
    d = 6 × 24
    d = 144
  Therefore, the distance travelled by the jeep is 144 km.
  The answer is B: 144km.

Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can use the formula N = N0 * 2^(t/k) where N0 is the initial number of water lilies, N is the final number of water lilies, t is the total time, and k is the doubling time.
  If there was exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. This means that N = 2^30.
  If initially there were 64 water lilies on it, then N0 = 64.
  We need to find t when N = 2^30 * 64.
  We can rewrite N = 2^(30 + 6) = 2^36.
  Therefore, 2^36 = 64 * 2^(t/2).
  We can simplify this to 2^30 = 2^(t/2).
  Therefore, t/2 = 30 and t = 60.
  The lake will be fully covered with lilies in 60 days.

Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9 am. So, it takes 4 hours to travel from A to B.
  Train N leaves City B at 7 am and reaches City A at 10:30 am. So, it takes 3 hours and 30 minutes to travel from B to A.
  Let's assume the 2 trains cross each other at x hours after 7 am.
  The time taken by train N to cover the remaining distance = (x - 3.5) hours.
  The time taken by train M to cover the remaining distance = (4 - x) hours.
  Since both the trains cover the same distance, we can use the formula Distance = Speed x Time to get the time they cross each other.
  Let's assume the speed of train M be S1 and the speed of train N be S2.
  Distance covered by train M = S1 * (4 - x)
  Distance covered by train N = S2 * (x - 3.5)
  Since both the distances are equal, we can equate them.
  S1 * (4 - x) = S2 * (x - 3.5)
  4S1 - xS1 = xS2 - 3.5S2
  4S1 + 3.5S2 = x(S1 + S2)
  x = (4S1 + 3.5S2) / (S1 + S2)
  We don't know the values of S1 and S2, but we can use the fact that the ratio of their speeds is equal to the inverse ratio of their travel times.
  The time taken by train M to travel from A to B is 4 hours, and the time taken by train N to travel from B to A is 3.5 hours. So, the ratio of their speeds is 4:3.5 or 8:7.
  Let's assume the speed of train M is 8x and the speed of train N is 7x.
  Then, x = (4S1 + 3.5S2) / (S1 + S2) = (4 * 8x + 3.5 * 7x) / (8x + 7x) = 31.5 / 15x = 2.1 hours.
  Therefore, the trains cross each other 2.1 hours after 7 am, or at 9:06 am (7:00 am + 2 hours + 6 minutes).
  The answer is None of the Above.

  Speed of N = 140/3.5 = 40 km/h

Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Thought:
  The sum of the weights of the 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons * 10 = 122 tons.
  After adding the heavy duty truck, the sum of the weights of the 11 vehicles is (12.2 tons * 10) + x, where x is the weight of the heavy duty truck in tons.
  The new average weight of the 11 vehicles is (12.2 tons * 10 + x) / 11.
  The new average weight is 2.6 tons more than the old average weight, so we can set up the equation:
  (12.2 tons * 10 + x) / 11 = 12.2 tons + 2.6 tons
  Solving for x:
  122 + x = 11 * 14.8
  x = 44.8
  Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 44.8 tons.
Action: Answer("E")

Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Thought:
  We know the mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay.
  We want to remove and replace some of the mixture to make the mixture contain equal quantities of sand and clay.
  Let's assume we remove x kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
  As a result, the amount of sand in the new mixture will be 30% of (10-x)kg + 100% of x kg.
  The amount of clay in the new mixture will be 70% of (10-x)kg.
  We want these two values to be equal to each other, so we can set them equal and solve for x.
  30% of (10-x)kg + 100% of x kg = 70% of (10-x)kg
  0.3(10-x) + x = 0.7(10-x)
  3 - 0.3x + x = 7 - 0.7x
  0.4x = 4
  x = 10
  Therefore, we need to remove 10 kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
  Answer: Answer("A")

Question: Find the total no. of distinct bike no.'s that can beformed using 2 letters followed by 2 no.'s. How many letters need to be distinct?
Choices:
  A: 74453
  B: 64543
  C: 74325
  D: 65000
  E: 97656
Response 0:
Thought:
  We have to form a bike number using 2 letters followed by 2 numbers.
  There are 26 letters in the English alphabet.
  We can choose any one of the 26 letters for the first letter and any one of the 26 letters for the second letter.
  Therefore, the total number of ways we can choose 2 letters is 26 * 26 = 676.
  There are 10 digits (0-9) that we can choose for each of the two numbers.
  Therefore, the total number of ways we can choose 2 numbers is 10 * 10 = 100.
  Therefore, the total number of distinct bike numbers that can be formed is 676 * 100 = 67,600.
  The number of letters that need to be distinct is 2.
  Therefore, the answer is not A, C, D, or E.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We need to find the total number of distinct bike numbers.
  The bike number is formed using 2 letters followed by 2 numbers.
  The number of distinct letters needed to form the bike number is 26.
  The number of distinct numbers needed to form the bike number is 10.
  We can use the permutation formula to find the total number of distinct bike numbers.
  The formula is nPr = n! / (n-r)!
  Here, n = 26 + 10 = 36 (total number of distinct letters and numbers)
  r = 4 (number of places in the bike number)
  So, the total number of distinct bike numbers = 36P4 = 47,376
  Therefore, no. of letters need to be distinct is 2.

  Therefore, Jill will need to buy 15 bottles of soda for a party in which 12 people are attending.

Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the length of the rectangular plot to be L and the breadth to be B.
  The perimeter of the rectangular plot is given as 340 meters. Therefore,
  2(L + B) = 340
  L + B = 170
  Now, we need to find the cost of gardening a 1-meter boundary around the rectangular plot. 
  The length of the rectangular plot with the boundary will be L + 2 and the breadth will be B + 2.
  Therefore, the area of the garden will be (L+2) * (B+2).
  The cost of gardening is given as 10 per square meter.
  Therefore, the cost of gardening the garden will be 10 * (L+2) * (B+2).
  Now, we can solve for the cost of gardening.
  Substituting L = 170 - B in the equation for cost:
  Cost = 10 * (L+2) * (B+2) = 10 * (172-B) * (B+2) = 10 * (-B^2 + 168B + 344)
  To find the maximum value of the quadratic equation, we can differentiate the equation and set it equal to 0:
  d(Cost)/d(B) = -20B + 168 = 0
  B = 8.4
  L = 161.6
  Therefore, the cost of gardening is:
  Cost = 10 * (161.6+2) * (8.4+2) = 10 * 163.6 * 10.4 = 17014.4
  The answer is A: 3400.

Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Thought:
  The merchant purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450.
  The rate of each kg of oranges was Rs. 450/90 = Rs. 5.
  The merchant sold the whole lot at a rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
  The selling price of 90 kg of oranges is Rs. (90 x 7.50) = Rs. 675.
  The profit made by the merchant is Rs. (675 - 450) = Rs. 225.
  The percentage gain can be calculated by (Profit / Cost Price) x 100.
  So, the percentage gain is (225 / 450) x 100 = 50%.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 50%.
Action: Answer("A")

  Therefore, the percentage gain of the merchant is 50%.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister and his father.
  Let x be Joe's age, y be his sister's age, and z be his father's age.
  We know that x + y + z = 100.
  We are also given two equations involving their ages in the future and in the past, respectively.

  In the future:
  When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now.
  This can be written as: 2(x+y+z) = x + 2z + 2(y + z - x)
  Simplifying this equation, we get: x = z - y

  In the past:
  When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father.
  Let a be the age when Joe's sister was as old as her father.
  We can write this as: z - a = 2(a - y)
  Simplifying this equation, we get: a = (2z + y)/3

  Now we have two equations in terms of z, y. 
  We can substitute x = z - y in the equation a = (2z + y)/3. 
  Then we can substitute z - y for x in x + y + z = 100. 
  This will give us one equation in terms of z, which we can solve for z.

  x = z - y
  a = (2z + y)/3
  x + y + z = 100

  Substituting x = z - y in a = (2z + y)/3:
  (z - y) + y + z = 100 - > 2z = 100 - a*3

  Substituting 2z = 100 - a*3 in a = (2z + y)/3:
  a = (100 - a*3 + y)/3 - > a*4 = 100 + y

  Now substituting a*4 = 100 + y in x + y + z = 100:
  z = 50 - a
  y = a*4 - 100
  x = 50 - a*3

  Therefore, z = 50 - a = 50 - (100 + y)/4.
  Simplifying this equation, we get: a = 32.
  Finally, substituting a = 32 in z = 50 - a, we get: z = 18.

  Therefore, Joe's father's age is 18.

Action: Answer("A")

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Thought:
  For every Heads flipped, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan. 
  For every Tails flipped, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  Let's assume the coin landed on Heads x times.
  Therefore, the coin landed on Tails (20 - x) times.
  Christopher gave $2x to Jonathan.
  Jonathan gave $3(20 - x) to Christopher.
  Since none of them won or lost any amount, $2x = $3(20 - x).
  Solving for x, we get x = 12.
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan when the coin lands on Heads.
  Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher when the coin lands on Tails.
  Let's represent the number of times the coin landed on Heads with X.
  The number of times the coin landed on Tails is 20 - X.
  Christopher wins 2$ X times and Jonathan loses 2$ X times when the coin lands on Heads.
  Jonathan wins 3$ (20 - X) times and Christopher loses 3$ (20 - X) times when the coin lands on Tails.
  The total amount Christopher wins is equal to the total amount Jonathan loses.
  2X = 3(20 - X)
  2X = 60 - 3X
  5X = 60
  X = 12
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Thought:

  Christopher gave away 2x dollars.
  Jonathan gave away 3(20-x) dollars.

  2x = 3(20 - x)
  2x = 60 - 3x
  5x = 60
  x = 12

Response 4:
Thought:
  Each time the coin lands on Heads, Christopher loses $2 and Jonathan gains $2.
  Each time the coin lands on Tails, Christopher gains $3 and Jonathan loses $3.
  The total amount gained or lost after 20 flips is zero.
  Let H be the number of times the coin lands on Heads and T be the number of times the coin lands on Tails.
  We know that H + T = 20.
  We also know that:
    -2H + 3T = 0 (because the total amount gained or lost is zero)
    -2H = -3T
    H = (3/2)T
  Since H and T are integers, we know that T must be even (because 3/2 is not an integer).
  The only even choice is 10, so we can substitute T = 10 to find H:
    H = (3/2)T = (3/2)(10) = 15
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 15 times.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let d be the distance between A and B.
  Let t1 be the time it takes Kevin to get from A to B.
  Let t2 be the time it takes Kevin to get from B to A.
  We know that d = 70t1 and d = 90t2.
  We also know that t2 = t1 - 3, since Kevin has 3 hours less to travel on the way back.
  At the moment when Kevin is 70 miles away from B, he has traveled 70t1 miles in total.
  We can set up an equation using the above information and solve for d.

Calculation:
  d = 70t1
  d = 90t2
  t2 = t1 - 3
  70t1 + 70 = 90(t1 - 3)
  70t1 + 70 = 90t1 - 270
  160t1 = 340
  t1 = 2.125
  d = 70t1
  d = 70 * 2.125
  d = 148.75

Answer: Answer("E") None of the above. 

Explanation: 
  The calculated distance between A and B is 148.75 miles which is not one of the available choices.
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's denote the distance between A and B as "d".
  Let's denote the time it took Kevin to get from A to B as "t".
  Let's denote the time it took Kevin to get from B to A as "x".
  We know that Kevin drove to B at a constant speed of 70 mph, therefore:
  d = 70t
  We also know that Kevin drove back to A at a constant speed of 90 mph, therefore:
  d = 90x
  We are given that exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. Therefore, at this point, he had driven a total of:
  d + 70
  We also know that he had 3 hours left to complete his trip at this point. Therefore, the time it took him to get from this point to A was:
  3 + x
  We can now set up an equation using the information above:
  d + 70 = 70(3 + x) + 90x
  Substituting d = 90x from the second equation, we get:
  90x + 70 = 210 + 160x
  70 = 70x + 210
  x = 1
  Therefore, it took Kevin 1 hour to get from B to A.
  Using d = 90x, we can find that the distance between A and B is:
  d = 90(1) = 90
  The answer is B: 90.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the distance between A and B is "d" miles.
  Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph, so he covered the distance of "d" miles in d/70 hours.
  Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph.
  So, the time he took to travel from B to A is d/90 hours.
  Kevin was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it, 3 hours before the end of his trip.
  Let's assume that Kevin reached B after "t" hours after he started his journey from A.
  Therefore, he started his return journey from B after (t - d/70) hours.
  Kevin traveled 70 miles in (t - d/70) hours and traveled the remaining d - 70 miles in (d/90) hours.
  We know that 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  Therefore, (d - 70) = 70[(t - d/70) - 3] + 90(d/90).
  Solving the above equation, we get d = 270.
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 270 miles.
  The answer is C: 270.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that there are 'x' employees in the organization.
  Each employee contributed 'a' amount of money.
  Therefore, the total amount of money raised is given by the product of the number of employees and the amount of money each employee contributed, i.e., x*a = 6 lakh.
  If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, then the new contribution per employee would be (a + 60).
  The new total amount of money raised is given by the product of the number of employees and the new amount of money each employee contributed, i.e., x*(a+60) = 6.24 lakh.
  We can use these two equations to solve for 'x'.
  From the first equation, we know that a = (6 lakh)/x.
  Substituting this value of 'a' in the second equation, we get:
  x*(6 lakh/x + 60) = 6.24 lakh
  6 lakh + 60x = 6.24 lakh
  60x = 24,000
  x = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let x be the number of employees in the organization.
  Each employee's contribution = total amount to be raised / number of employees = 6 lakh / x.
  If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, then each employee's new contribution would be (6.24 lakh / x).
  According to the problem, the new contribution is 60 rupees more than the original contribution. So we can set up an equation:
  6 lakh / x + 60 = 6.24 lakh / x
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
  The answer is C: 400.

### Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 98 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Thought:
Let the amount each nephew receives be x.
Then each daughter receives 4x and each son receives 5x.
The total number of recipients is 5 + 4 + 2 = 11.
The total amount of money distributed is Rs 8600.
We can set up an equation to solve for x and then use that value to find how much each daughter receives.
Equation: 5(5x) + 4(4x) + 2x = 8600
Solving this equation, we get x = 200.
Therefore, each daughter receives 4x = 4(200) = Rs 800.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Let's assume the amount each nephew received is "x".
  Each daughter received four times as much as each nephew, so each daughter received 4x.
  Each son received five times as much as each nephew, so each son received 5x.
  Total number of family members = 5 sons + 4 daughters + 2 nephews = 11.
  Total amount shared = Rs 8600.
  So, (5 * 5x) + (4 * 4x) + (2 * x) = Rs 8600.
  Solving the above equation, we get x = 200.
  Each daughter received 4x = 4 * 200 = Rs 800.
  Therefore, the answer is E: Rs 800.

The total number of people who will receive the money is 5+4+2 = 11.

The total amount of money received by the nephews is 2x.
The total amount of money received by the daughters is 4*4x = 16x.
The total amount of money received by the sons is 5*2x = 10x.
So, the total amount of money received by all the people is 2x + 16x + 10x = 28x.
According to the question, the total amount of money given is Rs 8600.
Therefore, 28x = 8600.
So, x = 307.14 (approx).
Therefore, each daughter will receive 4x = Rs 1228.57 (approx).

Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
  Let's say the maximum distance we can travel is d miles.
  To calculate the cost of the trip, we can subtract the initial cost of the first quarter-mile from the total cost.
  So, the cost of the remaining (d-0.25) miles is (d-0.25)*0.10.
  The total cost of the trip must be less than or equal to $8.50.
  Therefore, we can set up the inequality: 3.50 + 0.10(d-0.25) <= 8.50
  Solving for d, we get: d <= 12.75
  Therefore, the maximum distance we can travel is 12.75 miles.
